Northwest Inspection Notes

— By Our Special Correspondent Ya.

Miracles of the Desert 75

Anxi is far from the border of Gansu Province, controlling the vital transportation hub of Gansu and Xinjiang. Its territory is vast, larger than Zhejiang Province. Its residents are diverse and have historically been difficult to govern. In the past few years, after the ravages of Wu Yanzhang and Ma Zhongying, the local area has become impoverished and is in a dire state. Since last year, when Ma Zhongying led his troops to Xinjiang, the first regiment of the 298th Brigade of the 100th Division has been stationed there. Local order has gradually become stable, and the people's vitality can also be restored. In addition, Fan Yuancen, the director of the special tax bureau, has been actively contacting merchants in Xinjiang to ensure that new goods are still regularly transported to Anxi for trade with goods from Baotou and Suiyuan. From then on, the transportation between Gansu and Xinjiang can barely be maintained, and the commercial transportation outside the frontier is gradually showing signs of recovery. Ma Shou Xuan, the regiment commander of the stationed army, is strict in governing the army and kind to people. The border people praised him. Because the troops are stationed in various places, only one battalion and one artillery company are stationed in Anxi. At 8 AM on the fourth day of the reporter's arrival in Anxi, at the invitation of Regiment Commander Ma, the reporter, along with County Magistrate Xie and Director Fan, entered the barracks and saw that the soldiers were full of energy. All their actions, advances, and retreats were quick and organized. Especially when performing the division parade, a strong wind suddenly rose, and sand blew into their eyes, but the formation remained perfectly disciplined. Secondly, they were technically skilled. All exercises such as broadsword, boxing, bayonet, swordsmanship, stick fighting, and iron bar exercises were very flexible. Thirdly, the clothing was neat and tidy. Not only were the clothes, hats, and shoes all the same, but the length of the hair also had the characteristics of simultaneous haircuts during mobilization. Regiment Commander Ma is not only good at governing the army, but also very dedicated to local construction projects. Once, the reporter unintentionally mentioned to Ma that the troops stationed in a certain place were able to vigorously support local construction, personnel repairs, and afforestation, and achieved remarkable results. Later, when the reporter returned from Dunhuang, within a short period of ten days, the four main streets in the east, west, south, and north of Anxi City had become flat, wide, and tidy avenues. Water ditches were also dug deep on both sides in preparation for planting willows in the coming spring. Later, because the ditches were not covered with bricks, which was inconvenient for large vehicles to drive on, the previous effort was not different. The reporter immediately suggested filling them shallowly. If this kind of [goodness is followed, and evil is corrected] spirit can be fully developed, and the promotion of senior officials can be obtained, it will be used to implement the post-military land reclamation (especially since Longxi has vast land and sparse population, and a large army is stationed there, it is very suitable for land reclamation), then the effect will be even greater.

The reporter has been staying in Anxi for several days, but there is no good news about the road conditions to Xinjiang. The car from Lanzhou was originally intended to go to Dihua to transport intestines, but has also received a telegram from Dihua, instructing them to wait here for the time being. The reporter interviewed Xu Tiemin, director of the Anxi station of the Central Asian Airlines. According to him, aviation in Xinjiang has been suspended since September of last year, and it will soon be over a year. This is not only a very regrettable thing in terms of the future significance of Eurasian transportation, but also the losses suffered by border culture, commerce, and the company's own operations are also considerable. Xinjiang's specialties, such as gold, antelope horns, and musk, are always transported to the east by air by wealthy merchants to catch the good prices, resulting in all seats being fully booked every time they fly. Some people even book seats in advance or charter flights alone for more than 15,000 yuan. It can be seen that if this airline can be restored as soon as possible, it will be of great practical benefit in all aspects. According to the responsible person of the Post and Telecommunications Bureau, Xinjiang's postal service has been sluggish since the 21st year. On March 21 of this year, there was a letter from Hami. By April, it had been opened to Zhenxi, Muleihe, and Qitai, but it was interrupted again in early August. Only Hami can still communicate. As for Dihua and Southern Xinjiang, communication has been broken for three years. More than 190 large bags of parcels destined for Dihua from Hunan, Shanghai, Beiping, and Gansu are stored in the Anxi Post Office. It is said that there are also many stored in the Suzhou and Hami post offices. Most of the recipients of these parcels stored in the Anxi Bureau are Jin Shuren, the former chairman of Xinjiang. Jin has already settled in Taiwan, so it is also interesting to have the parcels waiting to be sent to Xinjiang. Xinjiang's telegraph service was interrupted in May of the 20th year, and telegraph and telephone services to Hami were finally opened in May of last year. On July 1st of this year, telegraph services to Dihua were also opened, which is really good news for transportation in the frontier. Since the road conditions to Xinjiang were unclear, I first made an inspection of Dunhuang. Dunhuang is 280 li southwest of Anxi City. Initially, I went out of the west gate and traveled diagonally to the southwest. The green willows and yellow wheat along the way were quite pleasant. The old Guazhou City, which was 40 li away, used to have more than a thousand households, but was destroyed in the Tongzhi War and only a broken wall remains, covered with camel thorns (a perennial shrub in the desert, thick and thick, with long and sharp thorns, which camels like to eat). Recently, I heard that a few warehouses were set up to store autumn grain, but I didn't see it. There are a few farm households on the east side of the road. It was very hot and thirsty. I bought water to drink, which was soaked in fennel. It is said that it is easy to get bloated in the desert summer, and drinking this tea can prevent epidemics. They firmly refused to accept the money I gave them. Twenty li further, I arrived at "Liugong". The weather was extremely hot, and I could not continue. I planned to find a place to stay, but people everywhere scattered, which was quite strange. I caught sight of a woman lying on the roof of a house and finally asked where the village chief was and went to stay there. The farmland in the village is calculated by household, with each household having about 60 mu. Each year, they pay three dan of wheat grain. Other tobacco tax, fines, and miscellaneous taxes and expenses are paid an uncertain number of times a year, and the amount varies. Ordinary clear water fields used to be more valuable than mountain water fields. Now, because the clear water fields pay three times more than the mountain water fields, families with fields would rather send them to others to cultivate and subsidize cattle carts, but only ask them to bear the grain tax. However, no one dares to accept it. Ma Zhongying once arrested 70 farmers here, and later each family spent 20 to 30 yuan to redeem 32 people. Those who had no money to redeem were all taken to Xinjiang and have not returned to this day. Therefore, the villagers

[Unintelligible characters] 76

Are extremely lacking. I set off from Liugong at six o'clock in the morning and entered the Gobi Desert, traveling along the south side of the small mountain for 70 li without seeing a tree or encountering a person. In ancient times, it was said, "I don't know where to stay tonight, there is no human smoke for thousands of miles in the flat desert," which can be used as a portrayal. There is a strange scene in the Gobi: from a distance, the blue air seems to be trapped in the sea, and the inverted shadows of mountains, rocks, and vegetation are in it, and some are floating in the sky. They appear and disappear, like sharks but not sharks. The illusion of a mirage is no more than this. As the car slowly advances, it moves leisurely to other places, step by step attracting people into the scenic spots, making them overwhelmed. Some say that this is the origin of the name "瀚海" (Han Hai). Others say that it is a phenomenon of miasma in the Gobi. In fact, it is a result of the difference in the density of air and the refraction of light. Near noon, the scorching sun is steaming, the artemisia grass is haggard, the color is green, and it shatters when touched. Dozens of gazelles flee from the left and right in groups, and their agility is unmatched. In the blink of an eye, they disappear into the distance. It is said that as soon as they fall to the ground, they can walk as well as their mothers as soon as their hair is dry, and the same is true for wild horses and wild camels (also known as single-humped camels). Therefore, in the land of mixed wolf and bear, they can still breed and reproduce. On the first two days of my trip from Anxi, it happened that Regiment Commander Ma returned from hunting and left me a gazelle with a firm and sharp horn that grew high on the head and bent slightly forward, unlike the cattle and sheep whose horns bay down on both sides (females have no horns). I was suffering from not knowing how to cook it, when County Magistrate Xie suddenly invited me to taste this thing. The meat is coarse and slightly grassy, ​​which does not seem as good as domestic lamb.

When I arrived at Tianshui Well, I saw many parked ox carts, either carrying melons, fruits, and grains, or carrying gypsum, fur, all of which were traveling at night and resting here, about to go to Anxi. There is only an ancient temple and a store here, specializing in watching the well water, which can get two buckets of wheat per month. The taste of the well water is extremely bitter and salty. It can be barely palatable after boiling and drinking hot, but it is very difficult to swallow when cold, and it is easy to get diarrhea after drinking it, so it is called "sweet water", which implies a meaning of begging and hoping. Yesterday, Secretary Du Jingshan kindly gifted me two bottles of canned fruit, which I firmly refused, but to no avail. Now, they are put to great use. After resting until four o'clock in the afternoon, the car continued to move forward. The road was still the Gobi. As the red sun set in the west, I encountered more than a dozen large carts in a row, and arrived at Gedagang Well and stayed overnight at midnight, traveling sixty or seventy li. Although the well water here is slightly better, there is nothing else except for a store. A certain traveler passed by here, unable to find food, and actually wrote the sentence "Tighten your belly and rush to Dunhuang" on the wall.

I set off on the third day and met a Taoist who had fled from Guchengzi, saying that since Ma Zhongying disrupted Guchengzi, the price of grain (the common name for grain prices in Gansu) has been high, and the locals are grabbing food, making it difficult to make a living, so he fled to Guan Nei. When the reporter passed through Suzhou, I saw a letter from a missionary who had just been sent to Xinjiang by the Catholic Church, which was even worse than what the Taoist said. However, he did not give up and continued to move forward, while the monks and Taoists of our country retreated into Guan Nei. In contrast, how can courage and cowardice be tolerated? Twenty li later, I passed a large salt lake of more than ten li in circumference, which naturally turned into salt. Looking from a distance, it looked like accumulated snow. The nearby residents freely take food. Forty li west of Dunhuang City, there is a Xiyanchi. This is Dongyanchi. There are two roads in the pool. The north road goes straight through the center of the pool. It can be walked on when it is frozen, and the journey is 10 miles shorter. The south road goes around the lake, and can be walked in all seasons. The road is 10 li longer. Xinhuzi is west of the lake and is 30 li from Gedagang. The two places look at each other, as if only a stone's throw away, but the route is deviated and the reeds are luxuriant, so people cannot go there. The walls of the houses in the city are connected to each other, the market is noisy, and the prosperity of commerce is only seen from Liangzhou in the west.

Chairman Chiang Returns to Jiangxi from Taiyuan via Wuhan 77

Soong Mei-ling and Kung Hsiang-hsi Depart for Nanjing

Yang Yung-tai and Others Travel South by Train

A dispatch from Hankou states: Chairman Chiang, having previously traveled north of the Han River, inspected the provinces of Henan, Shaanxi, Gansu, Ningxia, Hebei, Chahar, Suiyuan, and Shanxi. This lasted for over a month. Along the way, he summoned local military and government officials and addressed the masses. He received a warm welcome. After meeting with Yan Xishan in Taiyuan for several days, and because the campaign against the bandits in Jiangxi was progressing smoothly and the remaining bandits had fled their nests, Chiang urgently needed to return to Jiangxi to arrange for their pursuit and suppression. Coincidentally, a giant airplane from the Eurasia Aviation Corporation was inspecting the Northwest air route and passed through Taiyuan. He took the plane at 9:00 AM on the 11th to return to Jiangxi via Wuhan. He was accompanied only by his chief bodyguard, Ding Luwu, his secretary, Wang Rizhang, and three adjutants. Li Jingcong, the general manager of the Eurasia Aviation Corporation, and his deputy manager, a Westerner named Jie Peng, also came south on the plane. Madame Chiang Soong Mei-ling and Minister Kung Hsiang-hsi returned directly to Nanjing from Taiyuan. Secretary-General Yang Yung-tai and all the accompanying staff and guards took the train at 2:00 PM on the same afternoon to Shijiazhuang, and then traveled south on the Pinghan Railway. As Chairman Chiang's departure was abrupt, the military and government agencies here had not received any prior notification. In the afternoon, Deputy Commander Zhang Xueliang and Director He Chengjun received a telegram from Yang Yung-tai, stating briefly that the Chairman had flown to Jiangxi from Taiyuan at 9:00 AM that morning, but did not mention whether he would stop in Wuhan. At 3:30 PM, the giant Eurasia airplane arrived in Wuhan and landed at Wangjiadun Airport. After disembarking, Chiang originally intended to rest briefly before flying directly to Nanchang on the same plane. However, he received a telegram from Jiujiang reporting that the weather was unfavorable. They then went to Deming Hotel for lunch. Deputy Commander Zhang Xueliang, Chairman Zhang Qun, Commander Qi Peng, Mayor Wu Guozhen, and Director Chen Xihui successively came to pay their respects. At the same time, the Yong Sui warship was notified to raise steam and sail from the Jiangmian River in Wuchang Huijia Lane to the Sanbei Wharf to await orders. Chairman Chiang received each person individually and inquired in detail about military and government affairs. At 10:00 PM, he took a car to the Sanbei Wharf to board the ship. Zhang Xueliang, He Chengjun, Zhang Qun, Qian Dajun, Qi Peng, Wu Guozhen, Chen Xihui, Cai Mengjian, Li Jihong, Qiu Kaiji, and Tang Guozhen boarded the ship to see him off. The police department, public security bureau, and military police provided strict security along the route and at the wharf. Sailors from the Yong Sui warship also went ashore to assist. After Chiang got out of the car, he walked to the ship, thanking the people who were seeing him off and saying that there was no need for them to board the ship. After a while, as the ship was about to depart, Chiang reappeared on the deck, smiling and urging Deputy Commander Zhang and others to return early. At 10:15 PM, the ship set sail eastward. The people who were seeing him off gradually dispersed. The water journey to Xunyang is about 18 hours, and it is estimated that he will arrive in Xunyang at 4:00 PM on the 12th, and then take a car to Nanchang. Liu Xiang, the commander-in-chief of the bandit suppression in Sichuan, had originally planned to come east to meet with Chiang. The location was originally set in Hankou, but it has now been changed to Nanchang. Liu will take a plane to Hankou in the next day or two, and then transfer to Jiangxi to meet with Chiang to earnestly discuss with Chairman Chiang the issue of pacifying Sichuan and suppressing bandits. (11th)

Japanese Troops in Malanyu to Withdraw Soon 78

Our Security Forces Prepare to Take Over

Difficulties in the Takeover Have Been Overcome

A dispatch from Beiping states: The issue of taking over the Eastern Mausoleums in Malanyu seems to be nearing fruition. According to news from Malanyu a few days ago, the commander of the Japanese regiment stationed there, Miyama, convened a meeting of the responsible parties of the puppet army in the Eastern Mausoleums and local gentry to discuss the withdrawal issue. It was decided that the puppet army in the Eastern Mausoleums would begin to withdraw from yesterday (the 9th) and would complete the withdrawal by the 13th. Miyama himself is scheduled to host a farewell banquet for leaders of various agencies and local gentry tonight (the 10th). The Japanese army has also decided to withdraw outside the pass when our security forces enter to take over. The date for our security forces to enter the Eastern Mausoleums in Malanyu has been roughly set for the 13th. Whether there will be any temporary changes is currently difficult to say. However, it is more reliable that the difficulties in the takeover of the Eastern Mausoleums in Malanyu have been completely overcome. Only the handover procedures may be sooner or later.

After the Eastern Mausoleums are taken over by our side in the future, the issues within the war zone can be said to be entirely matters of cleaning up. It is said that the cleaning-up procedure will prioritize the crackdown on Japanese and Korean vagrants. The Japanese side has long agreed to crack down on Japanese and Korean vagrants, as most of the disputes in the war zone are caused by Japanese and Korean vagrants. There are many such cases in the past. If all the Japanese and Korean vagrants in the war zone can abide by the law, then all administrative construction in the war zone can proceed in an orderly manner, and there will be no reason for unnecessary disputes to arise. Therefore, after the establishment of the War Zone Cleanup Committee, it is currently preparing everything and will begin to proceed after the handover of the mausoleums. Su Mi District Commissioner Yin Rugeng visited Gubeikou on the 5th of this month to inspect the traffic conditions in the counties under his jurisdiction, together with Huo Shi, the director stationed in Gubeikou, and then went to Baimalan, Qiangzilukou, Caojialu, and other passes for inspection. After returning to Beiping, he told reporters this morning (the 10th) that about 20 li of the Great Wall between Baimaguan and Caojialu was demolished in the past due to the feng shui of the Eastern Mausoleums. Now, due to the so-called [Great Wall Line] relationship, it is necessary to survey it. Since it is called [Great Wall Line], the original city base should be the standard. When Yin talked about the Eastern Mausoleums takeover issue, he briefly stated that there was no problem with the takeover, and the date could be finally determined after meeting with Shibayama, the military attaché of the Japanese embassy. According to further investigation, Yin Rugeng and Shibayama will go to Malanyu around the 14th at the latest. Representatives from all parties of the Eastern Mausoleums Management Committee will depart within days and gather in Malanyu to participate in the takeover ceremony and begin work. (10th)

Ji Hongchang and Ren Yingqi Suddenly Attacked in Tianjin 79

Gunfire Suddenly Erupts Amidst a Game of Mahjong

Liu Shaoliang Killed, Ji and Ren Slightly Injured

A dispatch from Tianjin states: A bizarre homicide suddenly occurred at the Guomin Hotel in the French Concession of Tianjin at 7:50 PM on the 9th. Liu Shaoliang died on the spot, and Ji Hongchang and Ren Yingqi were also attacked and injured at the same time. They were sent to the French Hospital for treatment. The details of the incident are recorded below:

On the 31st of last month, a traveler came to the Guomin Hotel. A tea attendant led him to room 38 on the third floor. When registering in the hotel register, the traveler claimed to be Xu Jiyun from Beiping. After arriving at the hotel, he had many friends coming and going every day, and he often played mahjong. On the 9th, Xu Jiyun asked the tea attendant to move from room 38 to room 45 on the third floor. In the afternoon, he invited Ji Hongchang, Ren Yingqi, and Liu Shaoliang to gather in room 45, playing cards and chatting. Unexpectedly, at 7:55 PM, there were six or seven gunshots inside. Liu Shaoliang was shot several times in the head on the spot. Ji Hongchang was also shot in the right arm, and Ren Yingqi was shot in the hand. Liu fell to the ground and died due to the severity of his injuries. Ji Hongchang was less seriously injured. Gao Hongwen, the tea attendant on duty on the third floor, shouted loudly while chasing the murderer. At that time, Xu Jiyun also tried to go downstairs, but was stopped by Li Mingxin, the hotel manager. He immediately reported to the French Municipal Council. Many Chinese and foreign detectives arrived and carried the deceased Liu Shaoliang to the Xikai mortuary. The injured Ji Hongchang and Ren Yingqi were carried to the Xikai French Hospital for treatment. Xu Jiyun was taken to the bureau for questioning. According to Li Mingxin, the hotel manager, Xu Jiyun made two long-distance calls to his home in Beiping this afternoon (the 9th). His home telephone number is South Bureau 1404, and he lives on Tianma Temple Street in Beiping. This information was obtained from the Beiping telephone directory. When the incident occurred, I heard gunshots downstairs and rushed upstairs. At this time, the tea attendant Gao Hongwen chased down and shouted, ["The person running downstairs with a gun is here!"]. While we were chasing, the gunman and another person escaped from the side door without a trace. Xu Jiyun was intercepted by me at this time. We do not know what Xu Jiyun's occupation is, nor do we know the motive for the murder, etc. It is said that after the injured Ji Hongchang and Ren Yingqi were taken to the French Hospital, they were treated by doctors, and their lives are not in danger. It is also said that Xu Jiyun is the manager of a Beiping asbestos company, and it is also reported that the murderer abandoned his gun on 25th Road when he fled. (10th)

Jiang Wu

Autumn Harvest Conference Held in This County Yesterday 84

Yesterday (the 10th) at 2:00 PM, the autumn assessment conference was held in this county government. The attendees were County Magistrate Xu, various bureau chiefs, section chiefs, district chiefs, Yang Zichun from the county party department, Kui from the suspected property department, Wang Zuxun and Fan Zupei representing the landowners, and others. County Magistrate Xu presided over the meeting. Guan Rongceng from the Finance Department and Liu Jianguang from the Civil Affairs Department stated that the provincial government had decided to set the autumn harvest at 70%. The landowners argued that this year's drought in the county was severe, and the autumn harvest was less than 50%. The county government reported to the province that it was 57%, which was unsubstantiated, and requested the authorities to consider the situation and allow a reduction to provide relief. After repeated discussions, it was agreed that the autumn harvest this year would be 60%. However, the landowners were only willing to accept 57% and even left the meeting early, refusing to increase the percentage to show compassion.

Land Price Declaration Actively Underway 87

Since receiving the provincial order to postpone the declaration of land prices in Wuxi City for one month and approving the temporary suspension of land price tax collection, the office has been working very hard on land price declaration matters. In addition to setting a household-by-household declaration method and a work schedule, it is also limited to start from the 11th. The township heads and temporary staff were assigned to distribute declaration forms by district to implement household-by-household declaration, so as to complete all collections before the 30th of this month. Yesterday, the land price declaration office convened the township heads of the first district, as well as district staff such as Chen Songfu, and Jin Mahua, three instructors, to hold a conversation meeting in the county government conference room. 35 people attended the meeting. County Magistrate Yan gave a speech, stating briefly that the land price declaration is an important policy for land consolidation, and it is obviously two different things from the collection of land price tax. The provincial government has now clearly stated that it will postpone the land tax, and the purpose of the people's organizations has been achieved. Therefore, the land price declaration must be implemented without any doubt and should be promoted diligently so that it can be completed as soon as possible. There are several points that the staff should pay attention to: 1. The method of filling out the declaration form should be explained peacefully to the public. 2. If the district needs the assistance of the map, it can ask the county government to transfer the order for assistance if necessary. 3. If you encounter deliberate obstruction, you should report it to the county for severe punishment. He asked the staff to do the above three points well. Subsequently, the instructors gave separate instructions on how to fill out the declaration form and allocated the guidance time for each group. After the meeting, all the township staff set off to distribute the forms to the businesses for true reporting. Urban residents believe that during the period of political training, before the start of constitutional government, and the people have not enjoyed the four rights, Jiangsu Province is rushing to handle the land price declaration in Wuxi, which is obviously contrary to the Premier's will. Therefore, Hua Yi, Wang Zhiru, and others, totaling 1,574 people, filed a lawsuit with the Executive Yuan and at the same time published a notice to seek assistance from all sectors of the country.

Local News

Various Circles Held a Commemorative Meeting for the Premier's Birthday Yesterday 92

City Flags and Agency Offices Closed

More Than 500 Representatives Attended the Meeting

According to the Central News Agency, yesterday was the anniversary of the birth of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the Premier of the Chinese Kuomintang. At 10:00 AM yesterday morning, various circles in this city specially held a commemorative meeting for the Premier's birthday in the assembly hall of the Chamber of Commerce at Tianhou Palace Bridge. More than 500 representatives from various agencies, groups, and schools attended. The meeting did not end until 12:00 noon. The whole city hung flags to celebrate, and all agencies were closed for one day. All schools and factories also had a day off. The various situations are recorded as follows:

Meeting Order 1. Ringing the bell to start the meeting; 2. All stand in silence; 3. Sing the Party Song; 4. Pay the highest respect to the Party and National Flag and the Premier's Portrait; 5. Chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will; 6. Silence; 7. Chairman's report; 8. Speeches; 9. Shout slogans; 10. Ceremony complete, meeting adjourned.

The representatives who attended the meeting included Li Zhixiang from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Wen Ren'an from the Bar Association, Wang Zongjian from the Jianghai Customs Supervision Office, Zhang Menglin from the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Zheng Chengqing from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Yu Zhenhui from the Municipal Farmers' Association, Wang Hanyu from the United Association of Citizens of the First Special Zone, Huang Xianggu from the United Association of Citizens of the Second Special Zone, and Yu Yaoqiu and others representing the trade unions of Southern Goods, Musical Instruments, Textiles, Rubber, and Bookbinding industries, as well as more than 500 representatives from various schools and party departments at all levels.

Chairman's Report The presidium consisted of Wang Yansong (Municipal Party Department), Zhang Yuanruo (Municipal Government), Tao Chengqing (Municipal Chamber of Commerce), Zhou Xuexiang (General Union), Yu Hui (Municipal Farmers' Association), and Xu Zexu (Educational Association). After performing the ceremony, Chairman Tao Baichuan gave a report, stating briefly that the Premier was born in Cuiheng Village 46 years before the founding of the Republic of China. In his 61 years of life, the Premier lived every day in wind and rain, even in storms. The Premier studied medicine at a young age and used his medical career to promote revolution. Later, the number of revolutionaries increased, and the Premier became more motivated to organize parties and groups to overthrow the Qing Dynasty. Although the environment at the time was so bad and difficult, it was the Premier's great spirit that enabled him to overthrow the Qing Dynasty. However, after the founding of the Republic of China, Yuan Shikai declared himself emperor and Zhang Dong attempted to restore the monarchy in the past, and warlords usurped national power in the future, making the Premier's proposals difficult to implement. Later, during the period when Duan Qirui was in power, there was a move to convene a National Assembly. The Premier went to Beijing to participate, but unfortunately passed away in Beijing. We can draw the following conclusions from the Premier's life's work: 1. The Premier lived every day in storms, and his spirit of striving to overcome obstacles never wavered. 2. There was not a single day of mediocrity in the Premier's revolutionary process, and his revolution was not for himself or his family, but to seek the birth of freedom for China, the birth of the Chinese Kuomintang, and the birth of the Republic of China.

Speeches from Various Circles Chapter Yuanruo delivered a speech, stating briefly that the chairman had reported in detail on all the Premier's doctrines, theories, and spirit. I have some thoughts to report to you: 1. It was the birth of the Premier that led to the birth of the Republic of China. Although the Premier is dead, the Republic of China will never die because of it. The Premier's doctrine and spirit still exist and should be further promoted and expanded. However, the significance of the Premier's birthday is so great, but the general public seems indifferent on the day of commemoration. Not only that, but some people advocate high-profile criticisms, thinking that the current Kuomintang has become religionized, holding commemorative weeks every week, and holding commemorative meetings from time to time. It is important to know that all countries in the world must have several enthusiastic commemorations every year, such as Christmas, which all countries celebrate enthusiastically to commemorate it. Now people in our country are also emulating this practice, but they are indifferent to the Premier's birthday, which is a manifestation of the difficult and morbid state of the Chinese nation. The Premier said that power arises from thought. In the future, we should unify our thoughts and show a kind of power. On this occasion of the Premier's birthday, we should enthusiastically raise our interest to celebrate it. 2. The greatness and profundity of the Premier's teachings should be understood by everyone. Today, the Chinese people have a considerable understanding of the Premier's teachings, but it is limited to a few. According to the Premier's teachings, it can be divided into two types: 1. The origin of thought, such as the Three People's Principles and the Five-Power Constitution. 2. The application of thought, such as knowing is difficult and doing is easy, and the preliminary stage of civil rights. This is to enable practical application. Therefore, in the future, the Chinese people should not only understand all the Premier's theories, but also do it down-to-earth with the spirit of revolution. There is also Wang Hanliang's speech, the words are omitted.

Slogans and Taglines [Slogans] 1. All compatriots across the country unite; 2. Resist foreign aggression and wash away national humiliation; 3. Eliminate the Red bandits and appease the refugees; 4. Actively develop the Northwest; 5. Support the Chinese Kuomintang; 6. Support the National Government; 7. Support the Five-Power Congress; 8. Long live the Chinese Kuomintang; 9. Long live the Republic of China; [Taglines] 1. The Premier is the savior of the Chinese nation and the human race in the world; 2. The Premier's birthday is a memorial day for the development of the new life of the Chinese nation.

Belgian Envoy to Leave for Beijing Today to Preside Over National Day Celebrations 94

Naming Ceremony of the New King on the 15th

No Ceremony Held in Shanghai

According to the New Voice News Agency, Belgian Ambassador to China, Mr. Jules de Leurquin, will accompany his wife south to Beijing today as the new Belgian King Leopold III celebrates his first naming day anniversary (i.e., National Day) on the 15th of this month. (According to Belgian custom, the monarch's birthday is not observed as National Day, but rather the date of his naming.) They are expected to arrive in the capital tonight, so that on that day, he can host Chinese and foreign guests at the Belgian Embassy in Nanjing to receive congratulations. Afterwards, he will leave Beijing for Shanghai on the 16th. It is reported that the Shanghai Embassy Office and the Consulate General will not hold any ceremonies on that day, only raise the Belgian flag and close for a day of rest. King Leopold III, now 33 years old, is the eldest son of the late King Albert and succeeded to the throne on February 21 this year, after his father died climbing the mountain of Namur and his mother Queen Astrid was killed. Queen Astrid, formerly a Swedish princess, married in 1926 and had two sons and one daughter. The eldest, Princess Josephine Charlotte, was born in Brussels, Belgium, on October 1, 1927. The two sons, the elder named Baudouin, is four years old, and Albert is only one year old. The new king's sister is the current Crown Princess of Italy, and his brother, Charles, is 30 years old and holds the title of Count of Flanders.

He is expected to return to China at the end of the year. According to Mr. Shi, he had previously taught at various universities in Beijing, leading a leisurely life. However, after taking a position in the Ministry of Law two years ago, he found the official duties overwhelming and felt that his personal energy was insufficient. He sought to resign for rest. He is grateful for the understanding of the President of the Court, who approved his resignation and ordered him to take advantage of his leisure time to go abroad to study judicial affairs. Mr. Shi also believes that traveling abroad would benefit his body and mind, as well as increase his knowledge, so he readily agreed. If he gains anything in the future, he can also contribute it to the country as reference material. He plans to go to Japan first because Japan has enacted new laws in recent years that China does not have, and many of its old laws have also been revised. It is necessary to carefully study the results of their implementation in order to understand their advantages and disadvantages. Vice President Tan has already gone to study European and American countries, so Mr. Shi does not need to go to Europe and America again.

6th National Exhibition Opens Yesterday Morning 96

Yu Hongjun's Speech: To Save the Nation, First, We Must Strengthen the Economy

The Temporary Market Will Open Today Due to Incomplete Arrangement

The Shanghai 6th National Products Movement Exhibition, sponsored by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, held its opening ceremony at the Penglai Market in Xiaoximen at 10:00 AM yesterday. The temporary market will begin business today because the arrangement is not yet complete.

The Agenda of the Meeting: (1) Opening; (2) Music; (3) All Stand; (4) Presidium in Place; (5) Pay the Highest Respect to the National Flag and the Portrait of the Premier; (6) Chairman Respectfully Reads the Will; (7) Silence; (8) Chairman's Speech; (9) Speeches by Various Bureau Directors; (10) Guest Speeches; (11) Chairman's Response; (12) Music; (13) Photography; (14) Adjournment.

The representatives who attended included representatives from all walks of life, Mayor's representative Yu Hongjun, Municipal Party Department representatives Zhang Dafu and Xing Wan, Garrison Command Li Douchu, Security Office Wang Zhicheng, Yang Hu's representative Hui Zesheng, Finance Bureau Yuan Fang, Public Utilities Bureau Director Xu Peihuang, Public Works Bureau Jiang Sanping, Land Bureau Chen Jixi, Public Security Bureau Feng Shuju, Education Bureau Jiang Jianbai, Postal Administration Shen Lindan, Municipal Farmers' Association Ye Yi, Women's National Products Annual Meeting Lin Kecong, Citizens' National Products Promotion Association Wang Jiean and Xu Chengrou, and manufacturers' representatives and guests from all walks of life, totaling hundreds of people.

Chairman Yu Hongjun, Xu Peihuang, Li Douchu, Xing Wan, and Wang Jiean of the Presidium. After the ceremony was carried out as planned, Yu Hongjun first delivered a speech on behalf of Wu Tiecheng, saying that today is the opening of the 6th National Products Exhibition and that because Mayor Wu is holding a memorial service for the Premier's birthday at the Municipal Government in the city center, he will give a brief report on behalf of his brother. Holding a national products exhibition is the foundation for mutual cooperation. Now that the country is in trouble and the people's livelihood is declining, we must cultivate vitality in order to save the situation. Empty talk will not succeed. All countries in the world are currently engaged in competition and are looking forward to the outbreak of war. Political activities are very vigorous, and the outward development of trade is even more fierce. They dump overproduced goods into China. All countries in the world regard China as the best market, which is truly heartbreaking. Therefore, to save the country, it is not enough to talk about economic strength. To strengthen economic strength, we must promote national products so that money does not flow out. In the past, cosmetics alone drained hundreds of thousands of yuan. It is conceivable that other items also do this. To relieve the rural areas, we must reject foreign goods. Holding a national products movement to make the people of the whole country understand national products is not just about holding an exhibition once a year. Please pay attention to the manufacturers to compare the goods of the past five years with today's goods to see if there has been any progress and urge improvement. Many Chinese products are more expensive than foreign goods and of inferior quality. I hope that we will work together to improve the quality and lower the price so that they can compete with foreign goods without failing and encourage each other to save the country.

Xu Peihuang's Speech Public Utilities Bureau Director Xu Peihuang gave a speech, briefly saying that the meaning of promoting national products is very profound. No matter what you do, you must think from a small perspective. If you promote national products yourself, you must want others to use national products as well. You must gradually persuade relatives and friends, and then let relatives and friends persuade their relatives and friends, and you can gradually succeed. Today's national products exhibition is already the sixth one. The results of the previous five years seem to be very few because the public often takes using foreign goods as the main body and national products as the object, thinking that foreign goods are of good quality and low price. Now we must change this mentality. The first point is to strengthen our strength and study the quality, and appropriately reduce the price, focusing on small profits. The second point is to improve the goods so that buyers can see at a glance and there is no suspicion of mixing fish eyes with pearls. The third point is to cooperate with the government when the people's livelihood is declining so that the people can support themselves to buy national products and concentrate their economy to cope with the crisis. Finally, Jiang Jianbai, a representative of the Education Bureau, and Wang Jiean, etc., gave speeches, which are not recorded due to their length.

Market Operation After the speeches by representatives from all walks of life, the chairman gave a reply, saying that he was very happy that the 6th National Products Exhibition opened today and that representatives from all walks of life came to participate despite the wind and rain. He hoped that the manufacturers' representatives would go back and encourage each other to strive for excellence in order to achieve the goal of saving the country with national products. In addition, the original plan was for this drip irrigation field to start business yesterday, but due to the suddenness of the time and the incomplete arrangement, it had to be postponed until today to be able to operate.

City Police Chief Wen Hong'en Died in Hospital Yesterday 97

Funeral Procession at the Chinese Funeral Home This Afternoon

Vacancy Temporarily Concurrently Held by Mayor Wu Tiecheng

City Police Chief Wen Hong'en died of illness at the Huxi Sanatorium at 4:15 PM yesterday. His remains were immediately transferred to the Haige Chinese Funeral Home. The funeral procession is scheduled for 2:30 PM this afternoon. All municipal government agencies will fly flags at half-mast today in mourning. Details are as follows:

Suffering from Heart Disease with Ineffective Treatment Chief Wen had a strong physique, but when he served as commander of the 17th Division during the Northern Expedition, he was injured and suffered from heart disease and other ailments, which were not immediately treated. The root of the disease deepened day by day. This autumn, he suffered from dysentery, which caused the old illness to recur. His heart enlarged and his kidney disease worsened. He was admitted to the Sino-Western Sanatorium for treatment. After careful diagnosis and treatment by Chinese and Western doctors, he lingered for several months without significant effect. A week ago, he went to the Huxi Sanatorium and stayed in room 300 for treatment. He was treated until 4:15 PM yesterday, when the treatment was ineffective and he died in the hospital. His remains were immediately transferred to the Chinese Funeral Home on Haig Road.

Vacancy Temporarily Held Concurrently by the Mayor Mr. Wen was 45 years old. He is survived by a wife, a son, and two daughters, who reside at No. 5, Garden Fang, Jin Shenfu Road. Upon hearing the news, Mr. Wen's colleagues went to the Chinese Funeral Home to pay their respects. Mayor Wu and other bureau directors also went to offer their condolences. It is reported that Mayor Wu believes that the responsibilities of the Public Security Bureau are extremely important. In addition to immediately selecting personnel for appointment, Wu himself will temporarily concurrently hold the position during the transitional period. All municipal government agencies will fly flags at half-mast today in mourning.

Wen's Brief History Served Repeatedly in Military Positions Wen Hong'en, a native of Guangdong, served as a staff officer in the Guangdong Provincial Bandit Suppression Army Headquarters, a commander of the Second Regiment of the First Route of the Guangdong Army, an adjutant of the Fourth Battalion. In 1921, he was wounded in the Gaozhou campaign in Guangdong in support of Guangxi. In 1922, he was the adjutant and battalion commander of the Second Company of the Second Regiment of the Eastern Route Bandit Suppression Army. In 1924, he was appointed commander of the Second Regiment of the Guangdong Provincial Guard Army. In 1925, it was changed to the 50th Regiment of the 17th Division of the National Revolutionary Army, and he continued to serve as commander. Later, he followed Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek on the Northern Expedition and recovered Nanchang. He was promoted to major general and regimental commander. He was wounded in the Battle of Nanjing. After recovering Nanjing, he was promoted to division commander of the 17th Division. Afterwards, he fought in Jianghuai, Lu, and Hebei until Machang in Tianjin. After the unification of the North and South, the 17th Division was reorganized into the 16th Brigade, and he served as brigade commander. He was then transferred to serve as chief of staff of the 6th Division. In 1929, he served as deputy division commander and division commander of the 58th Division of the Army. He was then sent by the National Government to Europe for inspection and practiced in various French corps. In 1932, he returned to China and served as a military counselor of the Military Council, and a research committee member of the Infantry School. In September 1933, he was appointed to his current position and concurrently served as commander of the police headquarters of the bureau. In December 1933, he was ordered to concurrently serve as the director of the police training school.

The First Association Sells the Latest National Highway Map 107

The Chinese National Road Construction Association has been engaged in road construction for fourteen years. It has been found that the total length of highways built and open to traffic in various provinces and regions across the country has reached over 10,750 kilometers, and the number of planned constructions is increasing daily. In order to investigate the actual conditions of highways in various provinces, the association has sent special personnel to various provinces to conduct detailed surveys of local routes, including railways, mountain ranges, rivers, and other items. They have compiled the latest national highway map and cooperated with the Shanghai Xingdi Geographical Society, hiring experts to create precise drawings. The names of all provinces, cities, counties, and towns passed along the routes are listed without omission, and the Ministry of Communications' highway plan map, the Committee's seven-province highway map, and other information are attached. The map is printed in color on a large sheet of high-quality daolin paper. The map is about four meters long and five meters wide, folded into a set for easy carrying. It is reported that since its publication, the number of people going to order it has been extremely high.

The original letter stated: "[It has been found that the shelters for the poor in the city during the winter have been managed and operated by your organization in previous years, with remarkable results, greatly benefiting the poor. This year, the drought disaster in various provinces is severe, leading to the bankruptcy of rural areas and the stagnation of industry and commerce, resulting in an increasing number of unemployed people and the growing impoverishment of the poor, making it even more necessary to follow the previous cases. With the approaching winter, we are writing to request that you consult the previous cases, prepare early, and inform us of the progress of the preparations. This is what we hope for. To the Shanghai United Charity Organization, from the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau,]" It is reported that after receiving the letter, the organization decided to convene a meeting of all charitable organizations (22 in the city) at its office at 4:00 PM tomorrow to discuss the implementation of this winter shelter for the poor.

Mao Fuqing, an idler and self-proclaimed inventor, 40 years old, recently secretly manufactured counterfeit copper coins in lead at the front building of No. 11, Lane 100, Rue de l'Amiral Bayle, French Concession, selling them on the market for profit, disrupting the financial order. The matter was discovered by Bao Detective Xu Guilin of the French Concession Police Station. On the afternoon of the 24th of last month, at 5:00 PM, he rushed to the address, arrested Mao, and seized eighty counterfeit copper coins made of lead, a set of plaster molds used for manufacturing, as well as copper spoons, furnaces, lead materials, and other items. He was taken to the police station and sent to the Special Second Court. The police lawyer filed a public prosecution based on the crime of privately manufacturing counterfeit currency. After interrogation by Judge Wang Gangxu, the details have been recorded in previous reports. The case has now been concluded. The other day, Judge Wang presided over the first criminal court, ordering the defendant to be brought to court and sentencing Mao Fuqing to two years and six months of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment is confirmed will be used, with two days offsetting one day of imprisonment. The counterfeit coins and equipment seized in the case will be confiscated.

Kneeling and Crying to Persuade a Modern Woman 111

Passive Resistance to the Influx of Foreign Goods

The Industrial Society says that since the emergence of the kneeling petition group in Shanghai, it has attracted the attention of people from all walks of life. The members of this group persuade the people of the country not to buy foreign goods every day along the streets, and their work is very diligent. The reporter of the Industrial Society has received several letters from the members of the group reporting the progress of the work in great detail. Their patriotic enthusiasm and painstaking efforts are indeed commendable. A certain Mr. Wang, also a member of the kneeling petition group, knelt down at about 2:00 PM yesterday next to the Dongshengxiang fur shop in Fangbang Street, East Gate, and begged a vendor, a certain Mr. Yang, who was setting up a stall selling inferior goods, telling him that foreign goods are flooding our country's market and that if the people of the country do not quickly repent, the national situation will be even more precarious. For a time, passers-by gathered to watch, blocking the road. After listening to him, the vendor Mr. Yang discovered his conscience and said that engaging in this kind of business was really a last resort, otherwise he would starve to death. In the future, he will try his best to find a way and will not do this kind of business again for the time being, in order to fulfill the duty of a citizen. Member Wang then thanked him and left. He then passed by Dacheng Road near the Temple of Confucius, when he happened to see a modern woman with coiled hair, high heels, leather shoes,盛装艷服 dressed in full foreign goods, coming slowly from the west. When the member saw her, he stepped forward, knelt down on both knees, and cried to the woman, explaining his intention. The woman, seeing this uninvited guest, whose behavior was strange, was greatly shocked, suspecting that he was a madman pretending to be insane. After listening to him, she realized that he was advising her not to wear foreign goods. However, the woman not only did not know how to repent, but also said loudly, "Wearing foreign goods is my freedom, what business is it of yours?" The member was still kneeling and refusing to get up, earnestly persuading and stopping the woman from leaving, not stopping until she repented. At that time, while it was in a state of commotion, a certain Mr. Hu, a student from Fudan University, happened to pass by. He immediately stepped forward to explain to the woman on behalf of member Wang. The woman then knew that she was in the wrong and at a loss for words, blushing and replying, "I will not wear foreign goods again next time." At this time, member Wang stood up, thanked her, and left.

Kuang Zhongmou Sued by His Wife 113

Lawsuit for Unpaid Deposits of Over 20,000 Taels

Husband and Wife for Many Years Actually Meet in Court

Kuang Says He Did Evil in His Previous Life and Will Not Do Evil in This Life

Kuang Zhongmou, the owner of Penglai Market in this city, was recently sued in the local court by his second wife, Kuang Huiyueying, represented by lawyers Yu Sunxiu and Huang Tao, for failing to pay deposits of 28,000 taels of silver. Before the lawsuit proceeded, although relatives and friends came forward to mediate, the conditions of both parties were difficult to reconcile, so the husband and wife of many years inevitably met in court. After receiving the complaint, the court has commissioned Fu Xunwei to complete the investigation; the settlement is pending and further out-of-court conciliation has been arranged. The day before yesterday afternoon, Judge Pang Shurong specially opened the first court to hear the case. Both the plaintiff and the defendant arrived in court with their lawyers. First, Kuang Huiyueying testified that the 28,000 taels of silver she deposited with the defendant's Asia Eastern Company, opened under the name of Pei Ji, was not paid back, so she requested a lawsuit of 150 yuan, later increased to 250 yuan due to insufficient expenses until July of the 15th year of the Republic. After that, she stopped managing it and he managed the meals himself. Question: Was your money used as the profits of the Asia Eastern Company? In the fifth year of the Republic, the profits were over 20,000 gold, in the sixth year the profits were 120,000 gold, and by the public year, the profits reached 420,000 gold. Because I followed him to do business, I had taken out 5,000 taels from the deposit book. Next, Kuang Zhongmou testified that this Pei Ji deposit book belonged to him. All the rent until the Bingyin year was collected by her as household expenses, which could receive hundreds of yuan per month. Now this rent is collected by the accounting manager. Earlier, the plaintiff's uncle, Kuang, mediated and proposed to change the deposit in the book to Penglai Silver Company, and change the account name to Hui Yue Ji, and give the plaintiff 150 yuan of pocket money per month. He said that he could not accept this condition, so it was not resolved. The judge asked both parties, "You have been husband and wife for many years, and in the future, your money will belong to your son. Why bother with this lawsuit?" Kuang replied, "This is a matter of the previous life. I did evil in my previous life. It is difficult for me to fulfill one side of my family." The court ordered witnesses Zhang Jiuda and Ni Jingqi to the case. According to Zhang's testimony, after the reorganization of Asia Eastern Company in October of the sixth year of the Republic, he began to work as the deputy accountant in the company. The company was reorganized again in the ninth year of the Republic, and six shareholders withdrew, leaving only four shareholders. The company ended in the eleventh year of the Republic. In the seventh year of the Republic, the registered capital of the Hui Yue Ji account was 500 taels, and the profit dividend was 7,000 to 8,000 taels. Later, he went to Yingyou Company to work. Question: Do you know if there are registered accounts in Asia Eastern Company? Answer: He knows a thing or two about this matter. Kuang sold bonds and deposited it into the company. Lastly, according to Ni Jingqi's testimony, he entered Asia Eastern Company as the main accountant in the tenth year of the Republic. There were a total of four shareholders, and Kuang Zhongmou was the largest shareholder. The shares were split the following year. Question: Did the shareholders take out the dividends? Answer: They took it out. Question: What about Hui Yueying's 8,000 yuan? Answer: They took it out. Question: Was the deposit clear when the company ended? Answer: It was clear. Question: Does Asia Eastern Company have a Pei Ji deposit book? Answer: Yes, he had one, he was writing the book, there was a man surnamed Shen, who said to him, Kuang Guang said that he would give him a Pei Ji deposit book, this money was Mr. Kuang's own, it was the money he sold government bonds for. Question: What was the money used for? Answer: He was in charge of clearing accounts, and there were other people who managed the money in and out. Question: Did you also write the words "8% interest" on the book? Answer: Yes. The judge said that because there was still a need to call the owner for questioning in this case, it would be best to reach a settlement out of court and schedule another hearing. Then the court adjourned.

Zhao Xiren Sentenced to One Year and Four Months

When Wu arrived in Shexian County, A Duo was suffering from an epidemic due to the heat and died soon after. Wu returned to Shanghai alone and told A Duo's mother, Ding Xu, about the situation. Xu did not believe him and suspected that Wu and Zhao had colluded. She then hired attorney Ni Jiong to file a complaint with the criminal court of the Second Special District, accusing Zhao Xiren of seducing a minor girl and Wu Meisu of fraud. After receiving the complaint, the court summoned them for questioning and ordered Zhao to be detained and Wu to be released on bail. A document was sent to the Shexian County Government to investigate. Now, a reply has been received, confirming that Ding A Duo did indeed die of illness. Judge Xiong Huiping opened a court hearing and declared the case concluded, scheduling a sentencing date, which has been recorded in previous reports. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, Judge Xiong presided over the second criminal court and pronounced the verdict: Zhao Xiren was sentenced to one year and four months of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment is confirmed will be used, with two days offsetting one day of imprisonment. Wu Meigong was found not guilty. During the appeal period, Zhao was still remanded to the detention center.

Reaction to Sand and Gravel Merchants Continuing to Use Private Baskets 121

The Barge Industry Association Petitions the Social Bureau to Correct the Practice

The Coal and Stone Barge Industry Association of this city submitted a document to the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau yesterday, stating: "Members of the association have reported that when barges carrying stones from various factories in Suzhou and Hangzhou arrive in Shanghai and are unloaded to brokers for settlement of tonnage, the amount of cargo is only 80% of the original ship's cargo. The loss is enormous. It has been found that the diameter of the basket used to be seven feet and one inch, but now it has been changed to seven feet and four inches, an increase of three inches. Such exploitation of barge owners should be quickly corrected to maintain business." Upon receiving the document, it was noted that the system of weights and measures has already been promulgated by the government to ensure a uniform system and avoid disputes. All industries should abide by the new system. According to the previous statement, it is evident that some sand and gravel merchants are still using private baskets to exploit barge owners and dare to openly violate the system of weights and measures and practice their deceptive tricks. In this time of economic downturn, barge owners can hardly bear such significant losses. It is appropriate to submit this document to your bureau for review and approval, to convene the Shanghai Sand and Gravel Industry Association on a regular basis, send responsible representatives to discuss corrective measures, and uniformly use the public scale and baskets to maintain commercial transportation.

Special Article: Several Fundamental Issues of the Chinese Constitution, Speech by Sun Zhesheng, Speaker of the Legislative Yuan, Recorded by Fan Shiqin. 129

Location: Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA

Date: 7 PM, November 3rd

Chairman, comrades, I am here today at the invitation of the YMCA to talk about the issue of the Chinese Constitution. I think we must first ask: Does China need a constitution? This is a prerequisite question. At the same time as asking if China needs a constitution, we must also ask if China needs to build a new country, a modern country. Then, the importance of the constitutional issue will naturally be felt by everyone.

(I) The Constitution and the Modern State

The constitutional issue has really been a central issue in China for decades. We now want to study how China can maintain itself, how it can survive in this era. Probably everyone agrees that if China can reform and become a modern country, it must have various conditions. In this way, China can maintain itself. The most important condition for a modern country is the condition of the rule of law. Whether in China or abroad, if a modern country is to be built, everyone must take the rule of law as the basic standpoint. Before and even now, China cannot be said to have become a country of the rule of law. For thousands of years, China has only been a country of rule by man. What is the result? Needless to say, it is very dangerous. If there is a wise monarch, the country will have peace and the people can live in peace. Otherwise, the country will be fundamentally shaken. As the saying goes, "When the man exists, the government thrives; when the man dies, the government ceases." China has been like this for thousands of years. This is a country of rule by man, not a country of the rule of law. The present country advocates the rule of law, because the rule by man is to fundamentally shake the later country, while the country of the rule of law is not like this. Whoever should abide by the law does not change due to the change of people. The difference between the country of the rule of law and the country of the rule by man lies in this. Then, whether China needs a constitution means whether China wants to become a modern country, whether it wants to become a country of the rule of law. If so, it must have a fundamental law, and the fundamental law is the constitution. Whether China needs a constitution is really not a problem. China's urgent need for a constitution is very easy to understand now. Otherwise, do not reform China into a modern country, a country of the rule of law. Or, do not save the country and seek survival. Then we can do without a constitution. If we want to organize a modern country, to save the country, we must make our country a country of the rule of law. Therefore, I will first make this prerequisite problem clear to you.

(II) The Establishment and Process of the Constitution

The constitution really comes with the revolution. When a country comes to a dead end, it must have a revolution, and it must have a new constitution. China is a revolutionary country. Although the work of the revolution has not yet been completed, the result of the revolution is to build the foundation of a new country. In foreign countries, whichever country has a constitution, either a written constitution or an unwritten constitution. The latter is like the British constitution. Although the United Kingdom has not yet written a written constitution in black and white, it has various basic conditions that determine it. This basic condition is based on the changes in British politics and hundreds of years of history, which is an unwritten constitution. Apart from the United Kingdom, the rest of the constitutional countries have written constitutions. Those written constitutions are mostly based on revolutions. After the revolution, there is a constitution, or the old constitution is overthrown by the revolution and a new constitution is established. The Chinese revolution has been going on for twenty-three years now, and the Chinese revolutionary movement has also had more than forty years of history. However, until now, China's constitution has not been determined. The reason is that the revolution has not yet succeeded, so a perfect constitution has not been established. Since the Republic of China, although there have been provisional laws, and Cao Kun's era even had a constitution, none of them had good results, precisely because the revolution had not yet succeeded.

If the constitution is not based on the revolution, the constitution has no foundation, because the constitution is the people's demand and the foundation of the country. The drafting of the constitution by the current Nanjing National Government is to determine the various original principles and policies of the National Revolution over the past decades, and the basic conditions for nation-building, as a one-time solution. The constitution drafting work has now been completed. The constitution reform case was passed by the Legislative Yuan in three readings two weeks ago. This draft constitution can be said to have been successfully promulgated as the constitution of the Republic of China.

(III) The Issue of the National System

This draft constitution is based on the results of our Legislative Yuan's research and discussion over the past year. We feel that there are fundamental problems to be solved in drafting the constitution. These fundamental problems, first, are to determine what kind of country China is based on the history and theory of the revolution. The draft first stipulates that China is a country of the Three Principles of the People. This draft has been discussed and studied for one or two years before the Legislative Yuan decided on it.

Why is China a country of the Three Principles of the People? First, it is necessary to explain what the Three Principles of the People are, namely Nationalism, Democracy, and People's Livelihood. The purpose of Nationalism is to make China a nation that is independent and not subject to the control of a second country or second nation. The purpose of Democracy is to make China a democratic country. The purpose of People's Livelihood is to improve the economic and social system, so that the people of the whole country have the right to survive. Taking these three principles as standards, China must use the Three Principles of the People to be established and the status of the country can be maintained, because the Three Principles of the People are the principles of the Kuomintang, and the Kuomintang has created the Republic of China through decades of revolutionary movements, so the Republic of China cannot be separated from the Kuomintang's Three Principles of the People. Now, many countries in Europe have provisions in this regard, saying that such and such a country is a certain nation's republic. This kind of regulation is the same as our regulation of the Three Principles of the People. For example, like Soviet Russia, it is a socialist country, with considerable performance in terms of people's livelihood, so its constitution stipulates that it is a socialist republic. China is a republic of the Three Principles of the People and cannot be changed. But it is not to say that China is now a republic of the Three Principles of the People. In fact, the Three Principles of the People have not been fully realized, and the Three Principles of the People's Xu Family has not been established. We are only saying that the Three Principles of the People can be established in China. In short, the purpose is to make China a nationally independent country, not subject to the oppression of foreign powers. The Chinese government is a public institution of the people, produced by the people, and also represents the people, guarantees the rights of the people, and can find solutions to China's poverty and bankruptcy. Therefore, the Three Principles of the People are our ideal purpose. Taking this ideal purpose and fundamental policy as the essence of the Chinese constitution to determine China's national system is really without doubt.

(To be continued)

Spring Autumn

Xiaoxitian (Little Western Paradise) 131

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 4: Seeking a Cold Job with a Cup of Tea, Obtaining Old Money to Discuss Expediency, Cunning Officials Colluding in Groups

Guo Dunpin sat down, took half a puff of his cigarette, held it between his fingers, gestured to Li Shilian, and shook his palm into a small circle. With a mouthful of smoke left in his throat, he said, "In a word, the rehabilitation donation is a very good source of income. Just handle a small part of it, and over a year, you can always talk about the number of squares." Before Li Shilian could answer, Jia Duocai called from outside the door, "Brother Shilian, are there guests here?" Shilian said, "It's okay, he's my fellow villager. Please come in." Jia Duocai came in and saw Guo Dunpin wearing an antique bronze-colored blue silk lined robe, with a blue serge vest on the outside, and a section of a silver watch chain showing from a small pocket. His face was thin, but somewhat swollen, with a pale complexion. A felt hat was placed on the table, which was his "ding" (official hat). The faint cyan gray color was very much like a half-wilted lotus leaf. From these, it could be seen that he had a special hobby. After Shilian introduced them, he learned that one was a banker and the other had returned from Gansu after handling tobacco and alcohol taxes. Jia Duocai smiled, "Just now I heard you say that some errand can earn tens of thousands of income. In a place like the Northwest, it's not easy to get such a lucrative position, right?" Guo Dunpin laughed, "Since Mr. Jia is in the banking industry, of course he knows what the Northwest produces. To levy taxes on the most valuable product, wouldn't there be a rich income?" Jia Duocai nodded and smiled, "I understand what you're saying. But there's one thing, there are naturally many people who want to obtain such a lucrative position. For someone like Li Shilian, who is new here, to want to engage in such a thing, I'm afraid it won't be easy, right?" Guo Dunpin threw away the cigarette held between his fingers, lit a new cigarette, and took a puff. He smiled, "I think things depend on human effort. Things in the world are not that difficult to handle. Take me for example, I don't have any acquaintances in Gansu, but I still managed to handle tax affairs in Gansu for more than two years." (62)

Wedding Fireworks 132

— 19

Around the ninth and tenth months of the lunar calendar, probably because the climate is moderate at that time, many families choose auspicious days to marry their daughters; the people of Suzhou call it "Golden September, Silver October." Although customs for setting off fireworks at weddings may differ from place to place, everyone agrees that this is a way for the groom's family to show special respect to the bride. However, I think this is not just a way to show respect to the bride. Now let's talk about the situation of setting off fireworks in Taizhou and Shaoxing, and then add my assumptions to ask scholars who study folk customs for confirmation.

When a family in Taizhou marries a new bride, the sound of firecrackers is incessant. The new bride sits upright in the sedan, and people can stop her and judge her appearance at will. The sound of firecrackers must continue until the sedan arrives at the groom's house. In Shaoxing, the doorways of families with happy events often fire guns day and night. There is no fixed time or number of times for firing. Near where I live, a family has been having a happy event, and the sound of guns has not stopped for three days. In addition to the sound of guns, the sound of fine music can also be heard from time to time.

Studying the customs in these two places, I feel that setting off fireworks at weddings has at least some significance of ancient defense. Women are spoils of war. They can be plundered at will, which was a common occurrence among ancient tribes. The so-called "cannon" is also a tool for defense and guarding. Putting them together, the meaning is self-evident. When a family in Taizhou marries a new bride, the sound of firecrackers is incessant, which is a vestige of ancient vigilance. At that time, people feared that after plundering a woman, other tribes would come out to intercept, so they had to set off fireworks along the way. Similarly, in Shaoxing, families with happy events often fire guns in front of their doors, which is also a vestige of ancient vigilance. At that time, after people had plundered a woman and returned, they feared that the principal might be anxious and want to come and take her back; or they feared that others would be envious and want to come and rob her together. So they had to set off fireworks at the door from time to time.

The above is my guess, which is inevitably somewhat arbitrary, but it seems reasonable; I made this in the midst of the incessant sounds of guns nearby.

Strolling Through Wusong 133

— Nailing

Turning north from the right side of the newly built building on Waibaidu Bridge and coming down Tian Tong Road, you can find Wusong Road, which I am going to talk about now.

What is special about Wusong? You only need to ask your friends who wear Western suits, and you will know that it and Fujian Road, which specializes in buying Chinese-style old clothes, are "different songs with the same theme"; yes, Wusong Road is a place where shops that specialize in selling old Western-style clothes gather. Occasionally, there are a few pairs of old leather shoes on display, but you can't find old Chinese-style clothes no matter what. - If you want to buy old Chinese-style clothes, you can go to Fujian Road.

There are probably thirty to forty shops selling old Western clothes on Wusong Road. They hang oilskin coats and modern raincoats in front of their doors. Inside the shops, there are entire cabinets of old Western suits. Among these Western suits, there are distinctions of upper, middle, and lower grades. The upper grades are mostly the same as new, and the price is naturally expensive; for the middle grades, a full set of three pieces can be bought for sixteen or seventeen yuan; the lower grades can be bought for only seven or eight yuan.

When going to these second-hand shops, the first thing is to be able to recognize the goods. If you don't know the goods, you will buy a Western suit with the lining turned over as new. The second thing is to know how to bargain. According to custom, their prices are particularly high. For example, if you can sell it for ten yuan, he will say eleven yuan. You can only start bidding from six or seven yuan and slowly add it up to ten yuan. At this time, he can sell it to you.

Whenever it's the season change, like when you go to Wusong Road to take a stroll, you can see many modern young men picking out well-fitting clothes there!
