When Disarmament is Implemented 135

Royal Fragrance Drifting Record 136

— Original Author Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

Every building has a special atmosphere, ordinary houses are like this, and palaces are also like this; the bedroom palace in Shengjing (Mukden) is certainly different from the bedroom palace in the Forbidden City in Beijing. When we first arrived, we inevitably felt unfamiliar; fortunately, the eunuchs who had been sent ahead were very capable. Through their efforts to rectify the situation, as many of the unique features as possible were corrected, and even those that could not be corrected were not very noticeable.

The main body of this bedroom palace is a main hall, a very high and large main hall; although its area is not comparable to the bedroom palace in the Forbidden City in Beijing, it is much larger than the one in the Summer Palace. On both sides of the main hall, there are two side halls arranged like two wings, forming an inverted U-shape. There is a long corridor connecting the side halls and the main hall. Its construction is also very exquisite, with glazed tiles on the top, which can also be used when it rains; but because the position of the corridor is in front of the hall, to get from the side hall to the main hall, or from the main hall to the side hall, you must first exit the hall door and then walk past the gallery. You cannot pass through the inside of the house. In this way, we can understand that in fact, the Empress Dowager's bedroom palace includes three separate buildings, rather than a continuous row of buildings.

We followed the Empress Dowager to the main hall first. Because this main hall has a large courtyard in front of it, there is plenty of light; the side halls on both sides are far apart, and they do not block the sunlight of the main hall at all, and they themselves can also get plenty of light. This method of construction can be said to be very suitable for hygiene - The Empress Dowager took a look and expressed great satisfaction; especially for the achievements displayed by the eunuchs who had been sent ahead, she was particularly happy. Inside this main hall, there are a total of three rooms: the central one is considered the Empress Dowager's study, and the old lady works and rests here. (172)

The Scrap Paper Collector 137

— Shen Yu

This is a true story worth recounting. I record it to substantiate this publication. The story is as follows:

One morning, a very slight commotion arose in our office. This was the beginning of the story.

The reason was a certain Western woman, named Kikauff. She was a female employee of our company. After she arrived at the office, she immediately said to the office boy in that department: [“Did you find my things? I forgot a package yesterday, containing a pair of high-heeled leather shoes and a gold watch, wrapped in newspaper. I put it in the wastepaper basket, intending to take it back when I left the office, but I forgot. Did you find it?”]

The office boy then asked the wastepaper collector who was in charge of clearing the wastepaper baskets in that department. According to the wastepaper collector: [“Indeed, I saw it. But I have seen similar paper packages before, but when opened, they turned out to be banana peels or other fruit shells. So, this time I threw it away without opening it.”]

Although he said so, she remained suspicious that the Chinese were [“dishonest”].

The next day, an old man in ragged clothes—the one who every morning carried away a pair of large baskets full of scrap paper from our company—came with a package. He happened to ask the office boy. He said: [“Yesterday, I found this package in the scrap paper pile, containing a gold watch and a pair of high-heeled leather shoes. Knowing it belonged here, I have come specially to return it.”]

Thereupon, the office boy led him to Kikauff. He handed the package to her, and when she opened it immediately, she was astonished to find the original items. She took only a single two-cent coin from her purse and gave it to the scrap paper collector, who left, seemingly disappointed. Therefore, people were quite critical of her stinginess.

Since this incident, the dignity of us Chinese has been invisibly elevated a level in their eyes.

Personal Vignettes

Wu Shuangre of Yushan 138

— Yu Youqing

In the late autumn of Jiangnan, I thought of the novelist Mr. Wu Shuangre from my hometown.

Shuangre, named Xu, was a native of Dongting Mountain in Suzhou, who had lived in Changshu for several generations. More than twenty years ago, he taught at the rice industry elementary school in the southern gate of Changshu. He mostly wore a black vest year-round. He was a kind of oriental humorist, with some humorous flavor in both his speech and writing. His well-known works included "Shuangre Jue Jin," "Happy Couple," etc. "Karma Mirror" was his masterpiece. Later, he taught at Zhengyi Middle School in Nanjing and Anhui Public School in Shanghai. In Changshu, he founded the "Qinxin Daily" and also published "After-Dinner Clock," which were writings for amusement. He had a long novel called "New Water Margin," which included all the people in Changshu who knew him. Unfortunately, it was not completed; otherwise, it could have been read as a local history of Changshu. He went to Guangdong with Xu Benxiao and worked for some "Datong Daily." Due to acclimatization issues, he suddenly returned. He also organized a "Shuangre Club," appearing on stage in theatrical roles, making fun of the world. Later, he began tutoring students in Chinese language, seeming somewhat resigned to old age. At the same time, he also served as a reviewer for the "Qin Daily," publishing Gongsun Jian's novels, and also edited the "Lightning" for telegrams. He was troubled for a long time and failed to develop his talents, and has already returned to the earth.

He was a bohemian celebrity, with one foot impaired, and people nicknamed him "Wu Bo," like Iron-Crutch Li. He and the literary figure Mr. Jiang Zhifan can be called a perfect pair, because one was Wu Bo and the other was Jiang Kuaqiao. Both of these individuals possessed a sense of humor. He was very polite to people, not at all like an old-fashioned person. With long hair and a beard, he resembled a romantic artist, often drinking tea in the Xiaoyao You teahouse in Changshu, and chatting daily with the late epigrapher Mr. Zhao Guni, enjoying humor. Since the passing of his mother, perhaps due to circumstances, he seemed somewhat depressed and gradually declined. Last autumn, he sent me a couple of letters, asking me to find him a teaching position in Suzhou with a monthly salary of sixty or seventy yuan. Unfortunately, I was not skilled in socializing and failed to fulfill his request. Thinking about it now, I feel I have failed his trust.

He wrote a "Record of Customs of Haiyu," describing from the first day of the year to New Year's Eve, a very interesting notebook. Now it is very difficult to find in the market of Changshu. After he died, his son, Xiao Re, advertised in the Changshu newspaper, seeking his writings, perhaps preparing to publish a memorial work. Whether it can be published is also a difficult question. I heard that Mr. Sun Yusheng, the Seaside Poet, was very close to him and specially visited him in Changshu one autumn, but unfortunately, he was still teaching at Zhengyi Middle School in Nanjing at that time!

I have very few of his writings here, only a few letters and two poems, one titled "Yushan Small Chronicle" and the other "Seashore Flute Sound." He promised to revise and comment on "Seashore Flute Sound" for me, but now it will not happen.

Some people said that he liked women with bound feet, but I dare not believe this. Perhaps people were joking with him!

Autumn is deep, and as the plants of Jiangnan wither, I thought of a novelist with a sense of humor, who is already sleeping under the ground. Life is so fleeting, too quick!

The special reviews include Zhou Binglin's "Our Thoughts on the 18th North China Games," Dong Shouyi's "The Success of the 18th North China Games," Ruan Weicun's "A Brief History of the North China Games," Chen Yubo's "Grand Opening Ceremony of the 18th North China Games," Zhang Wenhao's "Men's High School Track Events," Liu Haiji's "Men's High School Field Events," Chen Wenhai's "Men's High School All-Around," Guo Zhenbang's "Men's Middle School Track Events," Mu Wenping's "Men's Middle School Track and Field," Luo Zhiying's "Women's Track and Field," Tian Yongqing's "Various Ball Game Championship Competitions," Lin Lisan's "National Arts Performance and Competition," Tao Zhongjie's "Closing Ceremony," and Chen Yingming's "My Sports Life." The training section includes Ruan Weicun's "New Track and Field Techniques," Shao Kexian's "The Life of an Elementary School Physical Education Teacher," and the editor's "Sportsman and Athlete." There are also four or five records and more than ten excerpts. The current issue is sold separately for 20 cents, and the annual special price is 2 yuan. Domestic postage is free, and foreign postage is an additional 2.2 yuan. During the one-year solicitation period, those who order the annual subscription of the newspaper will not only receive the four thick volumes of the "Sports Quarterly" newly compiled by the China National Sports Association, but also be able to predict the pole vault performance of jumping king Fu Baolu on December 1st at the Shanghai Municipal First Stadium. Those who predict correctly or closest to the correct answer will receive a scholarship of 300 yuan for first place and 200 yuan for second place, as well as sports equipment, art supplies, rulers, etc. The deadline is the end of November. This is truly a great opportunity for sports readers to subscribe to the newspaper. The company's store at No. 27, 4th Avenue also has the same price for subscriptions.

Method for Distributing Subsidies to Private Specialized Schools 152

(Nanjing, 12th Dispatch) The Ministry of Education has stipulated the method for distributing subsidies to private specialized schools and above. Starting from October, each school will submit a monthly claim and the funds will be distributed evenly by the Ministry of Education.

Jiangsu Provincial Social Education Organization Staff and Teacher Association Representative Conference 153

(Nanjing, 12th Dispatch) The Jiangsu Provincial Social Education Organization Staff and Teacher Association held its sixth representative conference in Nanjing on the 12th, chaired by Gu Renzhu. The conference passed resolutions that social education organizations should actively promote teaching to popularize literacy education and that the Education Department should be petitioned to: A) Establish provincial regulations on appointment limits, treatment standards, seniority pay increases, and retirement pensions for staff and teachers of small and medium-sized social education organizations before the Ministry of Education promulgates national standards. B) Amend the newly revised regulations on the protection of teachers and staff so that those who have served in an organization for more than three years should also be given special protection and continue to be employed. C) Issue a clear decree that teachers and staff who have continued to serve in an organization for more than seven years should be allowed to take a one-year sabbatical with full pay to travel and study in various places. D) The number of winter and summer vacation days for staff of provincial social education organizations should be the same as the number of holidays for secondary schools promulgated by the Ministry of Education in the fifteenth proposal.

Ministry of Education Interprets Elementary School Regulations 154

The Ministry of Education previously received a report from the Jiangsu Education Department, which was based on a request from a county magistrate asking for clarification on whether teachers meeting the criteria in Article 78 of the elementary school regulations could be hired as teachers in the senior division of elementary schools. The Ministry of Education has now instructed the Education Department that all those who meet one of the qualifications in Article 78 of the elementary school regulations and have passed the examination and verification may be hired as teachers in the senior division of elementary schools, without distinguishing between those qualified for the senior or junior grade level.

Agricultural Expert Xu Xuan Dies 157

Mr. Xu Xuan, the chairman of the Chinese Agricultural Society and a professor at Peking University, died of illness in Peking on November 9. Mr. Xu was a giant in the agricultural field, having engaged in agricultural education for more than twenty years. His students are all over the country and are well-known domestically. Mr. Xu himself was proficient in agricultural economics and published many articles. His recent book, "The Food Problem," is full of rich materials and is especially beneficial to the national economy and people's livelihood. Unfortunately, the book had just been published when he passed away. The agricultural community was deeply saddened upon hearing the news.

Soviet Union's Illiteracy Eradication Campaign 158

(Moscow TASS, October 7) The rapid reduction of illiteracy in the Soviet Union is one of the greatest achievements of socialism in recent years. From 1929 to 1933, the original 38 million illiterate people have now become literate. The illiteracy eradication campaign began during the Civil War, when Lenin ordered the organization of the National Extraordinary Committee for Illiteracy Eradication to carry out this work. The number of adult students in 1920-1921 was 1,158,000, while in 1932-33 it increased to 9,512,000. The table below shows the results of this campaign:

Year / Percentage of Literate People

1913 / 33.0

1920 / 44.4

1926 / 52.8

1932 / 90.0

Complete illiteracy has almost been completely eliminated. Today's work is to eliminate so-called semi-literacy. Women's education has developed extremely rapidly. In 1927-28, female students accounted for 39.5% of students in literacy schools. By 1932-33, they accounted for 58.3%. Among students in schools specifically set up for semi-literate people, women accounted for 39.1% in 1927-28 and 56.2% in 1922-33. The 1897 census indicated that only 13% of women were literate. The cultural level of ethnic minorities in the Soviet Union is increasing day by day. Currently, 68 ethnic groups use the new Latin alphabet. The number of literate people in Azerbaijan has increased from 7% in 1925 to 52% in 1932, Uzbekistan from 10% to 52%, and Kazakhstan from 4% to 31.5%.

Jinda Alumni Association Cables Ministry of Education to Grant Preferential Treatment to Deceased Professor Li Shicen 161

Requesting Reference to the Precedent of Liu Fu of Peking University

A One-Time Grant of 10,000 Yuan for Relief

Mr. Li Shicen, a famous Chinese philosopher, passed away in his Shanghai residence on the 28th of last month. Scholars across the country were shocked and saddened by the news. Throughout his life, Mr. Li devoted himself to research and did not engage in production. Apart from his academic pursuits, his circumstances were extremely bleak. He was bedridden for more than a month and borrowed money for medical expenses. After his death, there were no funds for funeral expenses. His friends, such as Guo Yilin, managed to raise funds to cover the costs temporarily. Mr. Li left behind children who are still young. The expenses for their future life and education are nowhere to be found, leaving them crying and wailing. Friends and relatives are saddened. Yesterday, the Shanghai alumni association of National Jinan University sent a telegram to the Ministry of Education, requesting that the precedent of the late Professor Liu Bannong of Peking University be followed and that preferential treatment be given to Mr. Li's family, with a one-time grant of 10,000 yuan to Mr. Li's family to comfort the deceased and relieve the orphans and widows. The original telegram is recorded below: Urgent, Wang Shijie, Minister of Education of Nanjing, My alma mater Professor Li Shicen, is a leading philosophy expert in China. His more than twenty works are complete and substantial. People in the academic circle have long been aware of this and do not need us to make any further claims. Moreover, Mr. Li devoted his life to academic pursuits. He served in the education sector for more than ten years. This summer, in order to complete his works such as "History of Chinese Philosophy," he overworked himself and died for the sake of learning. The members of this association believe that he has taught at Jinan for more than three years with outstanding results and is truly commendable. In addition to participating in the memorial service to express our condolences, we have learned that Mr. Li was devoted to research and did not engage in production. His circumstances after his death are extremely bleak. Not only does he owe thousands of yuan for medical treatment and funeral expenses, but his wife and four children have no means of support for their future life and education. Therefore, we dare to humbly request your Excellency to follow the method of providing relief to Mr. Liu Bannong and provide relief to Mr. Li's family with 10,000 yuan, so that the living can work hard in academics and the deceased can rest in peace. Your Excellency upholds education and respects academics. Since you have provided relief to Mr. Liu Bannong before, we believe that you will not leave Mr. Li Shicen behind. We eagerly await your instructions. Shanghai Alumni Association of National Jinan University,

Telegram from Jinan Alumni Association in Japan: To the Funeral Committee of Li Residence, Jinan University, and to the family of the deceased, Mr. Shi Cen suddenly passed away. The philosopher has withered away. We have lost our mentor. We are deeply saddened. We send our condolences by telegram. Jinan Alumni Association in Japan

Outline of Provisional Measures for Student Internships in Jiangsu Normal Schools 163

The Department of Education Orders All Counties to Transmit and Comply

The final examination for graduates of Jiangsu Normal Schools will be decided by the Department of Education. Each school should end the academic subjects before the spring break and hold the graduation examination on schedule. The graduation examination will be held within one week after the spring break. After the examination, the internship will begin. After the internship is completed, the results will be reviewed to determine whether they are qualified or not. The Department of Education also divides the student internships of normal schools into three categories: observation internship, trial internship, and teaching practice, which are distributed in the first and second semesters of the final academic year, and plans the first semester of the final academic year and the first half of the second semester as the observation internship period, and after the final examination to the end of the semester as the teaching practice period, and drafts the outline of the provisional measures for teaching student internships in normal schools. The Ministry of Education has now printed and distributed the outline of the measures to the education bureaus of each county for transmission to the affiliated normal schools and affiliated primary schools for joint compliance and reporting. Those who do not have affiliated primary schools should immediately designate excellent local primary schools for teaching student internships (outline omitted).

Grain: Rumors of New Australian Wheat Contracts Lead to Sudden Decline in Wheat and Flour Markets 180

Flour Market: After the morning opening, the market for all months presented a consistent and stable appearance, with foreign wheat quoted at Chicago at -0.04 to -0.10 yuan and Canadian at -0.08 to -0.10 yuan. At the time of opening, sentiment among both industry insiders and outsiders was quite good, and mills were reluctant to sell, so the market for all months gradually improved, rising by 0.01 to 0.02 yuan compared to the previous week. However, at the afternoon opening, the market atmosphere suddenly changed drastically due to rumors that mills had contracted for another ship of Australian foreign wheat, or perhaps two ships, with prices rumored at 4.80 yuan or 4.90 yuan. This caused sentiment to weaken significantly, and mills immediately started selling, with outsiders following suit. Prices for all months suddenly fell by 0.03 to 0.05 yuan compared to the morning market. However, the current month slightly improved due to some replenishment by mills, while distant months remained stable and weak. As a result, the current month fell by 0.04 yuan, February fell by 0.035 yuan, and March and April fell by 0.025 yuan.

Wheat Market: After the morning opening, the market initially showed stability, then signs of declining. Foreign wheat was quoted at both Chicago and Canada at -0.04 to -0.08 yuan to -0.10 yuan. At the time of opening, trading for all months remained quiet. The market was slightly better by 0.01 to 0.02 yuan as sellers held back. However, at the afternoon opening, the market was initially stable, but later fell sharply due to the sudden decline in the flour market and rumors of continued contracts for two ships of foreign wheat. The market atmosphere weakened significantly, and prices fell across the board. The near-term prices saw greater declines due to mill activity. Future trends will depend on the price of foreign wheat and exchange rates. As a result, the current month fell by 0.06 yuan, December fell by 0.06 yuan, January fell by 0.05 yuan, February fell by 0.03 yuan, and March fell by 0.01 yuan. The spot wheat market remains stable, with 10,000 bags of Shandong Xuzhou Guide wheat opening at 3.90 yuan. They were borrowed by Lingfu Fengfuxin Da office.

Chicago wheat prices are strongly influenced by robust international market conditions. Continued drought in the Southwest region has further boosted prices recently. However, improved conditions in Argentina are slightly unfavorable to the market. Increased participation in trading from outside parties.

Red Grain Greatly Devastated by Japanese Army After Fall of Northeast 181

—Prices Remain Firm, Soybean Prices Rise Again—

This year, the production area for red grain (紅糧) has been greatly reduced because the Japanese army forced villagers to live forty "li" (里) outside the railway line before they could plant, so production is only about 50% to 60%. Therefore, the production price is rising daily, and transportation is not profitable. Spot supply for inspection is tight, and the market cannot meet demand, so prices are soaring. Yesterday, the market spot supply was only two cars of red grain. They were transported by Pinggu and Hexing separately and were used to cover previous short positions. Seeing the market strength, merchants immediately resold one car at 3.55 yuan. Another car of spot goods for delivery in two or three days was sold at 3.46 yuan. Three cars for delivery in two weeks were initially quoted at 3.42 yuan, but the price continuously rose via telegraph in the afternoon, further tightening the market and reaching 3.48 yuan. Therefore, the grain market is quite strong. Soybean prices also rose due to increased production costs and tight spot supplies. Sentiment is optimistic. Yesterday's market saw a rise of 0.04 to 0.05 yuan compared to last week. Total trading volume was 12 or 13 cars of various soybeans, destined for Changzhou, local streets, inland regions, and export factories.

Page 15

Free Talk

On Writers 189

— Xin Ren

Discussions on writers are not new, but they are particularly prevalent this year. The magazine "Literature" (文學) alone has discussed five or six writers. The fact that the writers being discussed are our contemporaries adds to our interest. However, if we pay close attention, we can immediately find important significance in this phenomenon.

In past discussions of writers, we have rarely found anything satisfactory. Some are out of context, forcing interpretations; others abandon science and nitpick over words. In reality, writing about writers is not an easy task. The author must have broad knowledge: generally in social science, specifically in art and literature. Most importantly, they must deeply understand the creative process of the writer being discussed.

We can say that discussions of writers are a special form of literary criticism. It is a type of criticism that expresses literary history in a comprehensive form. On one hand, it analyzes the writer's thoughts in their works, elucidating their historical realization and their attitude towards "life." These thoughts and attitudes are hidden beneath the cloak of imagery. To reveal them, we must use both methods: a "microscope" and a "telescope." Closely linked to analysis is evaluation.

Evaluation is what humans are said to be born with. But scientifically speaking, this is because humans are purposeful social practitioners. Unlike bees and ants, human actions pass through consciousness and are guided by it. Humans set correct goals based on realistic possibilities and act towards those goals. This setting depends on evaluation. Of course, analysis includes evaluation, and evaluation includes analysis.

Applying this principle to discussions of writers means that they not only explain what the writer is like but also judge what the writer will become or should become.

Needless to say, the author's position and method are paramount. A discussion of a writer not only examines past creations but also guides ongoing and future creations. If the author's position is contrary to the objective development of history and the method is contrary to the correct principles of science, then the above tasks cannot be fully accomplished.

The occurrence of all social phenomena, although caused by historical development, must be based on social necessity. The current prevalence of discussions of writers should be viewed in this light. What makes us feel gratified is that most current discussions of writers follow the above path. This phenomenon is by no means accidental.

Our literature has swept away the clusters of mandarin duck and butterfly fiction (鴛鴦蝴蝶), eliminated the ranks of talented scholars and beautiful women, and is moving forward step by step along the winding path of historical necessity. It is now reaching a new stage. It is exploring reality, expressing reality, and clarifying the major cells that have already developed on its body. Through this reckoning, it can learn some "ways to nourish life" to achieve beauty.

The current prevalence of discussions of writers, and the fact that they are prevalent on the path of science, tells us the above important meaning in itself. We offer our constant efforts to it as a gift to its "new life."

Thinking About Other Things From Inventions 190

— Ren Baige

Recently, newspapers carried two astonishing news items: one was a new invention in aviation, and the other was the successful testing of a death ray.

These inventions and successes are actually not new. They were revealed in various newspapers a long time ago, so why should they be treated as astonishing news now? However, precisely because it seems like World War II is about to arrive, and these inventions and successes can be used directly or indirectly as weapons of killing, they are particularly startling. Journalists should be the most perceptive people in the world. Can we ask them not to carry this as astonishing news in the newspapers?

According to the newspapers, the new invention in aviation is simply a major revolution in aviation history. It has already been adopted by the French Air Force and can make the French Air Force dominate the skies. The success of the death ray test was also led by the French Army, but the inventors are the German Kailaus and the Frenchman Christmas. Unlike the new invention in aviation, which is entirely the work of French scientists, it is still unknown which country the inventors will dedicate this new weapon of killing to. Perhaps they will use it as a tool for world peace.

France has always been a country with a dominant air force. Now that it has this newly invented aviation technology, it can naturally make its air force dominate the skies. However, the unfortunate thing is that the death ray is not necessarily owned by France. It is said that the death ray can completely disable humans who encounter it. If a giant machine emits a light of five million candlepower, it can completely disable enemy aircraft because the pilot will immediately become stiff and die upon encountering the light, and the aircraft will naturally fall. Although the new aviation technology invented by French scientists can make aircraft fly very stably in the air, rise and fall without danger, and is entirely based on automatic mechanisms, it still requires a person to sit on it and press the buttons. Upon encountering the death ray, it will completely lose its effectiveness. If France does not secure this death ray, it will be difficult to dominate the skies with its air force.

Unfortunately, there are still many scientists desperately inventing new weapons of killing. Now is the time when World War II is about to arrive. All imperialists are expanding their military equipment as much as possible, and scientists have always served the imperialist warlords. It is only natural for them to invent new weapons of killing for the imperialist warlords. The main thing is how to transfer these new weapons of killing to the hands of those who oppose imperialism and use them as weapons to eliminate the war. This is the most urgent step at present. Naturally, we must fundamentally demand that other scientists who oppose imperialism invent new weapons to eliminate the war. That is to say, inventing what weapons is not the problem. The problem is for whom to invent them and what to use them for. From this, we can see the proper path a scientist should take at present. Therefore, even the inventors of the death ray should not immediately be given a bad name.

According to the tone of the journalists, this death ray, which has not yet been contributed to any country, may be used as a tool for world peace. Although this is an unfulfilled prayer, we cannot help but hope that every scientist will walk this path. We especially hope that every scientist will first recognize which countries are truly seeking world peace, and then contribute everything to it.

However, recently French scientists have also tested piloting unmanned aircraft with radio waves. It is said that with this new invention, aviators can sit safely in the office, holding the radio switch in one hand, and arbitrarily direct the movement of distant aircraft, and this will soon be realized. In this way, naturally the death ray will have no way to deal with the aircraft. Because the power of the death ray can only completely disable or immediately stiffen and kill humans who encounter it, but it cannot destroy the unmanned aircraft itself. As a result, radio-controlled aircraft will still dominate the skies.

I think, then many scientists will invent a tool to cut off the radio waves and completely negate the effectiveness of the radio-controlled aircraft. This reminds me of the formula in our general novels of gods, monsters, swordsmen, and heroes: if you have a magic weapon to subdue me, I will have a magic weapon to subdue your magic weapon; if I have a weapon to defeat you, you will have a weapon to defeat my weapon. The Monkey King was able to make a big disturbance in the Heavenly Palace because he had the ability to transform into seventy-two different forms; if it were not for the Buddha's palm being able to restrain his somersaults, I am afraid that the whole world would have been turned upside down by him in one morning. However, fortunately, it is the process of this formula; otherwise, it would be a small matter for the Monkey King to turn the world upside down long ago. At most, it would only shorten the enthusiasm of those who read Journey to the West. The most unfortunate thing is that humans would only have to be slaves to the privileged few who possess a weapon of killing forever.

However, the process of this formula has now reached the time when it should end. The author of Journey to the West only wasted a little ink to put together this formula and make people spend many useful hours. We also feel that it is too uneconomical; and now there are still many scientists who do not hesitate to sacrifice the lives of all mankind to put together this formula. Are we still going to let it go on? The prehistory of mankind should end, and all human abilities should serve the happiness of mankind itself. At the beginning of the real history of mankind, mankind first ended all disputes between humans and applied all its abilities to disputes with and overcoming nature. At this time, all scientists will no longer compete with each other to invent new weapons of killing to subdue or defeat others. Naturally, this formula will be cancelled invisibly. Why don't we make all scientists quickly end the invention of new weapons of killing?

Passing Thoughts 191

— Ding Yishan

I advocate that a lie that does no harm to any party, but benefits one or both, should be told when it is necessary to lie.

I have examples among my friends: a woman in labor lost her beloved husband. She asked others about her husband's condition, and they said he was well, even though he had already entered the earth. Telling her the truth would likely result in two deaths. Telling her later, when it was safe for her to hear it, would not be too late. Another is a close friendship where a female classmate is passionately in love. Lying in such situations is excusable.

Today, I was taking a photo outdoors with a friend, having just adjusted the aperture. A completely unrelated person asked us to take a picture for him. Honestly refusing would have embarrassed him too much. Being poisoned by the need to save face, we had no choice but to consider his feelings. He knew nothing about photography. Fortunately, we had already taken eight shots and wound the film past. My friend pretended to take a picture for him. He asked if it was taken well, and my friend said it was. He wanted my friend to give him a copy, but my friend said it might not develop well, that the picture might be bad, but if it was good, he would print one for him. Thus, this unrelated person was happy without expecting a photo. We remained unrelated people.

On the way back, my friend felt sorry for him. I thought he was not to be pitied. The pitiable ones are those who know there will be no result but still seek help from others.

The Night at Han Shengjia's Pottery Village (Part 1) 192

— Sheng Huanming

Beneath the veil of night, it was pitch black...

Apart from the rumbling of the carriage wheels, everything was as silent as if dead. The night was already old. People were silent in the carriage, enduring a stifling hunger, staring straight ahead, waiting for the destination they longed for to appear. But before their eyes was only a vast, dark expanse...

The driver cracked his whip in the air, [Crack!] sending out a clear, sharp sound. He pointed the whip towards the distant side and said, [That's Han Shengjia's Pottery Village.]

It seemed there was still a yellow flicker of light in the direction the whip indicated, and the carriage was shaking violently. Rubbing tired eyes, the light could no longer be found.

[Am I seeing things?] I thought.

[Crack!] The carriage sped up a little. Leaning out, I carefully peered at the place the driver had just indicated. The wind carried the wild howls of dogs; sure enough, a cluster of darker outlines squatted not far away.

[It's really not a big village...] I thought with a slight disappointment.

Then, two flickers of light could be seen. People perked up, stretching their lazy waists and rubbing their bellies, entrusting their fatigue and hunger to the place with the flickering three or four lights.

It was a small village of twenty or thirty households. With a rumble, the carriage stopped in front of a door with a visible firelight. Knocking on the door, they peered inside through a wide crack. Suddenly, the inside of the house turned pitch black very quickly.

[Hey, we're asking for lodging, what are you afraid of!] The driver wiped his face and shouted inside. But after a moment, the inside remained silent...

[—Hey...] Impatient, he banged on the door forcefully.

[We really don't have anything!]

[We're asking for lodging—only grandsons would lie to you!]

[Ah, how many of you are there, where are you from?]

[Baotou. Important guests from Baotou—open up!]

[Warm, open up] Another old voice.

The door opened, and an old man struck a match, shaking it to light an oil lamp. Under the dim, struggling lamplight, he anxiously sized up the guests outside:

[Bosses, find another place!]

[They're students, not bosses, don't worry, we'll pay tomorrow, it'll be alright, these gentlemen are all students.]

One by one, they moved their luggage inside. Each patted the dust off themselves and continuously ran into this small mud house. These types of houses were commonly seen in recent journeys: every part of the house was covered with yellow mud, and at its lowest point, only one person could stand nearly upright. People who stretched could touch the roof. Including the original three people, there were thirteen heads coming and going inside the small house. It seemed exceptionally crowded.

[Is there anything to eat? We haven't eaten anything for most of the day.]

One of the householders, a thin woman with a pale face, looked at the two guards who came with them as if frightened: [We haven't eaten anything all day either, bosses!]

Amidst many disappointed and surprised eyes were some looks of disbelief. They stared blankly at her face; their faces; then, without any ideas, looked around the house; empty pots, cold stove, a half-covered water tank with six bowls and several pairs of chopsticks on it, besides these, nothing else could be found.

Silently, they scratched their heads, and the group sat and lay down on a kang on the east side. The guard, sent especially for them, who had a collapsed nose, patted the box on his side and sat down beside them.

[Don't lie, who would eat your food for free, we'll definitely pay tomorrow—right?]

[We're not lying, bosses, we really don't have anything at all.]

The Wandering Swordsman (5) 193

— Lu Fen

He had a very good fishing rod, but he didn't catch many fish, maybe one or two. He rarely came back empty-handed.

On the rare clear morning, passing by the thatched hut extending at the foot of the city wall, one could always see [Xiang Fu] sitting on the riverbank, leaning against a willow tree, holding the fishing rod, gazing into the distance across the reeds. His head, deeply covered by a tattered hat, swayed constantly, and a smile floated on his mushroom-like face, as if bowing to the herons standing in the water.

The river could be considered a small stream, barely able to accommodate a flat-bottomed boat. It snaked out from the ironworks, forming a pond here. Reeds grew luxuriantly, and lotus flowers and reed catkins scattered with a faint fragrance, obscuring the pedestrians and the acrid floating dust on the right. Passersby on the bridge would often stop, mocking the strange old man, [Xiang Fu]. But he never paid attention to them. Something made him young, luring him thousands of miles away.

Only when he noticed that a fish had taken the [float], and raised the rod, but the hook was empty, would he start grumbling angrily while putting an earthworm on the hook:

[...Unreasonable...Despicable...]

No one would believe he was fishing.

After re-immersing the hook in the water, he looked into the distance again. His forehead smoothed out because of happiness. Maybe because he saw red clouds, he suddenly shouted loudly, as he hated rain the most. Just thinking about rain would make his spine tingle. How would he spend such a gloomy day! He wouldn't even dream of it. He would pour white liquor straight into his belly.

He watched a school of small fish gathering on the bank, chirping and chasing a yellow leaf, and he laughed. He said loudly:

[It's you, huh? This dragon is still hard to subdue, like a dragon!]

Supplement to the Shanghai Shenbao

Talking Points

Flies 194

— Tianshe

To glue the linings for my wife's cotton shoes, I didn't cover the paste pot, which attracted two flies. Silently, they were just licking at the mouth of the pot. Waving them away didn't work; they seemed greedy and insatiable. I used the tip of my fountain pen to stab at them, piercing their abdomens and killing them. They lay dead on the table, and I felt proudly self-satisfied. Unexpectedly, my wife strongly objected, saying that the flies at the end of autumn and the beginning of winter were already half-dead and their senses were so dull that they had lost the ability to spread germs and would no longer harm people. Killing a [dead tiger] doesn't make you a towering hero, does it? You are supposed to be a scholarly and reasonable man.

I was subjected to this barrage of sarcasm from my wife. I knew her words were correct, but I was still not willing to concede. How could a dignified man be [put down] by a woman? Of course, I had my reasons:

[Regardless of whether it is harmful now, in the past, its [crimes are obvious]. How many deaths are on their bodies? Don't you remember that the Chongming man who pushed a cart next door to your house died of acute koleragical spasm, along with his entire family of seven, after eating a dead fly—also, didn't I have diarrhea for three days and three nights because I touched food after swatting flies? Often, epidemics throughout a village or city are initiated by flies, which are no less harmful than floods, ferocious beasts, drugs, or red bandits. We can't let them go just because they are old and weak, pardoning their past crimes of killing. You women are always soft-hearted. You must know that if they survive these seasons, they will become killing demons again.]

My wife was afraid of stirring up my anger, so she didn't argue further. However, I was still indignant.

How fierce, how arrogant, how cunning the flies of summer are. On a grand scale, they cause death to fill the fields, threatening homes. For example, if you lose sleep at night because of bedbugs and want to make up for it during the day, a fly will land on your nose and buzz incessantly. Just as you are about to raise your hand to strike it, it already gets the news and enters your ears and eyelids, eventually preventing you from being able to [sleep soundly by the north window]. Their behavior goes beyond [destroying nine generations of your family].

However, summer passes, autumn comes, and winter arrives again. Those who were once rampant bow their heads, become docile and dull, to the point of being like this. As the saying goes, [When fortune comes, the wind carries the Prince Teng Pavilion; when fortune departs, thunder shatters the Temple of Felicity Stele]. Observing flies, one can understand this.

Miscellaneous Writings on the Deceased 195

— Juefu

The Drummer

Anyone who has lived in Beiping for a while, except for a few well-off people, is probably familiar with the [drummer].

The [drummer], I think, is indeed a close friend of impoverished gentry and poor young men. At dawn, he carries two large baskets and holds a small, one-inch drum in one hand and a drumstick about half a foot long in the other. He slowly walks through one alley after another, knocking, "de, de, de..." If someone wants to sell antiques or jewelry, he buys them; if someone wants to sell household goods, he buys them; if someone wants to sell scrap copper or iron, he buys them; if someone wants to sell torn clothes or old shoes, he buys them... The things he wants to buy are very diverse. Whether they are for fun, for use, or discarded as waste, he does not refuse. A group of impoverished gentry families has received a lot of help from him.

If you have traded with him once or twice and he has sensed your weakness, knowing that you are someone who has a hard time making ends meet, as soon as you hear the "de, de, de..." sound, you don't even need to open your mouth. He will come into your residence and ask gently: "Do you have anything to sell?" If you are not so poor as to lack the necessities for eating and using, you will naturally feel annoyed and disgusted by his persistent inquiries, and you will inevitably scold him a few times and send him away. But if you don't even have money to buy cakes, when you see him coming, you rummage under the bed and search in the chests, looking carefully in the corners and on the bookshelves... If you find some broken shoes, old clothes, old newspapers, or glass bottles that you never paid much attention to, you will feel as happy as if you had found some treasure. When you take out the goods, even if they are not worth much, he will not leave immediately because he doesn't like them. He will always gently raise the price step by step until both parties are satisfied, which is much better than pawnshop clerks who often discourage you with a few unpleasant words. Wouldn't such a person seem amiable to poor young men?

The [drummer]'s business is very prosperous. Every day, just sitting in the residence, you will hear the "de de de..." sound at least ten or eight times. The reason for its prosperity, I think, may be precisely because it shows the decadence and decline of the old capital. Sometimes, I even suspect that this sound may be the death knell of this ancient city!

All Trades in the City are Depressed, But This Man Thrives 196

— Yian

Much Ado About Chinese Courtesy on the Tram 197

— Chui

The day before yesterday, I took the Shanghai-Hangzhou slow train from Songjiang at 3:05 PM to Shanghai. I got off at the South Station and immediately boarded the No. 4 tram from Gaochang Temple to Nanyang Bridge. At that time, the third-class car was already crowded. Although the first-class car was also full, it was not too crowded. I saw a person occupying almost two seats, with plenty of space on both sides, so I squeezed in to sit on one side because I had been walking with some difficulty. I didn't greet the person next to me because there was already space and there was no need to greet them.

Someone next to me, A (with four or five companions), got angry. He sneered and said: [It's ridiculous, do you have to sit here?]

I stood up and replied: [If you were sitting here, I might as well sit there.]

Someone else, B, chimed in, saying that I didn't [greet them] when I sat down, as if commanding people to move, which was absurd.

I said, I don't know your name, so I don't know how to [greet] you. I only know that you sit where there is space on the tram and I don't understand the rules of [greeting].

Another person, C, also made a sarcastic remark, saying, [Do you expect us to get up and give you our seats when we see you coming? How unreasonable! The Chinese don't understand courtesy.]

I said, I didn't know about [Chinese courtesy]. Now I know that when you sit on the tram, you must [greet] and [apologize] to the person next to you before you can sit down. Is this [Chinese courtesy]?

Another person, D, explained from the side (this one was the oldest of the four, about forty years old, and spoke with a little less anger): [For example, on the train, if there is no space, you must [greet] the person sitting first and ask them to make some room. It's the same on the tram.]

I wanted to argue with them further, but I thought I had eaten my fill and had nothing better to do than to bicker with these people. My energy would be wasted. But these gentlemen seemed to know something about [Chinese courtesy] and didn't seem completely uncivilized, so I thought about this so-called [Chinese courtesy].

He occupies more than two seats on the tram by himself. When he sees many people, he refuses to make room unless someone [greets] and [apologizes] to him. If you don't greet him, he will push you. Is this [Chinese courtesy]?

On the train, I often see one person occupying two or three seats and lying down to sleep, regardless of whether there is enough room for the other passengers to stand. He doesn't care and sleeps soundly until someone [greets] and [apologizes] to him and asks him to get up, then he slowly sits up. Is this [Chinese courtesy]?

Later, I thought that these people were still good. If they had been impolite and punched me, wouldn't I have suffered? I am thankful that these gentlemen still understood [Chinese courtesy], so I didn't suffer a big loss. Congratulations, congratulations.

East, West, South, North 198

— Sanduo

It's too hard to eat this year. However, being a person is even harder, especially for us young men.

The crime of [youthful exuberance] seems to be tied to your head from birth, not allowing you to move at all: If you raise a hand, that hand is not raised properly. If you lift a leg, that leg is not in accordance with the rules. It would be best to send you to a desolate island or an ancient temple to be a monk for three years!

Pan Hongsheng died, and many people called him a patriotic person: many people shook their heads and sighed that he was too young and impetuous, and that his death was not worth regretting (?!)

Natural disasters and man-made disasters, national affairs are deteriorating day by day, and who among the people does not want to catch up and save China, but there are many ways to save the country: dancing, chanting scriptures, the so-called ten years to grow a tree, ten years to teach, no matter what, everything must be done slowly. But he used a bomb to kill a traitorous merchant, thinking that the country would be saved in this way. Is it that easy?

Not that it is time to make judgments, no matter how people shake their heads, he is always a patriotic person, and it is still worth it to be so hot-tempered. If even this little bit of anger disappears completely, it really makes people afraid to think about it!

The Intellectual 199

— Jieren

To put it more elegantly, intellectuals are [scholars]. If you think that's too old-fashioned, then call them the [knowledge class]! But aren't we advocating [popular language] this year? Compared to those, [intellectuals] is the more common term!

Since ancient times, intellectuals have been the most respected: among the four classes of people [scholars, farmers, artisans, and merchants], intellectuals sat in the first chair. Because intellectuals are saints (?), and intellectuals will be officials in the future, they should be respected by everyone. So, [Even if the descendants are foolish, books must be read], if the ancestors in heaven have a spirit, once they pass the imperial examination, they can glorify their ancestors, gain the praise of the villagers, and be respected by everyone. If so, isn't this life fulfilling and the way to be human exhausted? Otherwise, at least he is an intellectual, a [literary family], which is not enough to be proud of.

Now it's different. Intellectuals have fallen from their thrones.

What good are intellectuals?

That's what people say. Indeed, intellectuals are of no use: [They can neither tell fortunes nor carry burdens]. At most, they can sell manuscripts and be literary beggars. But intellectuals still put on their arrogant airs, thinking that they are people who have read books, and that these wild things are not worth mentioning! [A scholar can be killed, but he cannot be humiliated], and [Starving to death is a small matter, losing integrity is a great matter]. If you take off this ragged gown, won't you lose face and status? That's something you'd rather die than do!

But now it's really different from before! Everyone says: [Farmers, workers, merchants, students, soldiers]. At least they show some face, only demoting them by three levels, without kicking them to the bottom. At the time, a confused] person said to his brother in a letter: [Scholars are at the bottom of the four classes, and it is impossible to be at the bottom of the four classes!] Although these words boosted the morale of others and diminished one's own prestige, they were nonetheless prescient. However, most intellectuals are mistaken by books. They only know how to hold books, shake their heads, and hum in a high or low voice: [In books there are houses of gold, in books there are jade-like beauties]. In this way, intellectuals can only isolate themselves from the world and live in the world of their own minds!

Shanghai's Private Elementary Schools 200

— Younong

Indeed, the importance of elementary school education cannot be denied. Our China knows its power, and all European and American countries attach importance to it. As a result, schools have sprung up, slowly from national, provincial, and county schools, and private individuals have also set up schools. Apart from opening up a way to make money, it can also be seen that Chinese people are enthusiastic about education.

In Shanghai, due to the large population and the relationship with the concessions, private schools are particularly prosperous, especially elementary schools. I myself have mixed in private schools for a few years. Although I am not a complete expert, I dare say that I know more than an outsider. Now I will write what I know to serve the readers.

The decoration of a store is very important for its business. Setting up an elementary school in Shanghai is of course the same. Although private elementary schools do not have sufficient funds like official elementary schools, they have to save in various places and decorate the school buildings a little more beautifully. This will not only overwhelm [competitors], but also attract customers.

Regarding teaching methods and [child psychology], they are rarely studied, because there are many [competitors]—although not as door-to-door and household-to-household as cigarette paper exchange and pawnshops, the number of so-called [lane elementary schools] in Shanghai is also considerable!—In this serious situation, they have to change their tastes and shift the research on [child psychology] and teaching methods to research on [parent psychology]. For example, which types of people live in this area, and they have to suit the tastes of these types of people, and change the subjects [according to local conditions]. For example, several elementary schools in a certain district do not have labor, art, singing, or physical education, but supplement them with English and classical Chinese.

The treatment of teachers is an exception everywhere, so this cannot be put in the example. In various aspects, such as taking care of capital, decorating the facade, etc., they have to calculate on the teachers' salaries and ask them (or her) to work hard, even to serve on a half-empty stomach. Otherwise, if you don't do it, then please leave. Anyway, you are not the only one who is unemployed. If you have money, are you still afraid that you can't buy goods?

It is also unsightly not to have female teachers. This is because women are gentle and very suitable for teaching children. At the same time, face is also very important. How can a school not have female teachers? Therefore, the conditions for hiring female teachers are even more stringent than those for men. However, readers should not misunderstand that female teachers are also vases.

What is it like in terms of training and teaching? The low salaries of teachers make their (or her) lives insecure, and the number of class hours per week is always more than thousands of minutes. They (or she) also have to correct papers after class. Their spirit is limited, and of course they cannot have good teaching methods to use in the classroom.

The place and equipment for physical education are even more out of the question. In addition to the classroom, the student recreation area is the alley. Shanghai's land is like gold. Where can they rent a sports field and purchase sports equipment for money?

Novel

Liu Desheng in Jiangxi (5) 201

— Wan Guoan

(3) What Division Was Forgotten

The big, dark fellow arrived at a dilapidated ancestral hall and, led by two guys with Mauser pistols, entered the tiled house in the front. Inside the house sat two thin military officers, who immediately scowled as soon as he entered and asked:

[Which division of the Japanese army are you from?]

[I forgot.]

[Bullshit—you forgot your division headquarters?]

[I've been a soldier for seven or eight years, and I've never figured out which division I'm in. I remember which company, which battalion, which regiment, and which squad I'm in.]

[Do you think the White Army is good?]

[I'm not a soldier of the White or Red Army; I'm a soldier of the National Revolutionary Army.]

[This guy is really stupid; he doesn't even understand this. Shoot him!]

[I don't care if you shoot me, but I don't have a wife yet!]

[If you tell the truth, I'll give you a wife.] The questioner said with a smile.

[Tell what?]

[How many months have you not received your pay?]

[We take cash after discounts. We receive our pay every month. Can we still delay pay when fighting bandits?]

This big, dark fellow acted like a fool, leaving those two guys not knowing whether to laugh or cry. They had to think of another clever way. That night, the big, dark fellow was led to another small room. He ate two big bowls of dry rice and a bowl of vegetable soup, finally filling his stomach. Then he lay down on a broken wooden bed, his eyes watching the dim oil lamp on the wall. Just as he was about to [doze off], a young woman came in from outside. The big, dark fellow's eyes lit up, and he perked up considerably. A strange energy flowed through his body, diminishing his desire to [doze off].

The young woman sat next to the big, dark fellow with a grin. The big, dark fellow immediately felt a heat rising from under the young woman. He really couldn't restrain himself. At this time, the young woman leaned even closer, which made the big, dark fellow almost unable to breathe from the heat.

[Comrade: We are really going to be good!] she said, extending her right arm over the big, dark fellow's shoulder. The heat from her face also gradually warmed him.

[Huh! Good! Be good!] The big, dark fellow answered half-understandingly.

[Tomorrow we will hold a welcome rally to welcome you to join the Red Army. Please give a speech.]

[What? What is a speech?]

[It means talking to the comrades.]

[Say what?]

[I'll teach you first, and you can go on stage tomorrow and say it.]

[I can't learn it.] The big, dark fellow grinned.

Amateur Mailbox

— Editor

In addition to individual replies, this column will publish excerpts of readers' letters and welcomes readers to express their opinions on various issues. The editor will select and publish them in this column to fulfill the responsibility of criticizing society and to serve as the voice of the people. However, please note the following points when submitting articles: 1. Authors are responsible for their own articles; 2. Issues must be related to the lives of the general public and should not be too specialized; 3. Provide your real name and address (this column can keep it confidential), and the published name will be determined by the submitter; 4. The editor has the right to make changes to the submitted articles, and those that attack individuals or are close to flattery will not be published; 5. Manuscripts will not be returned regardless of whether they are published; 6. No payment will be given.

To Liu Renjing, Biyun, Pingying, Shi, Zhang Yanfan, and Liu Jianying: Please provide your contact address so that we can reply.

Mr. Yang, from Jiangsu, is 24 years old, speaks both Beijing and Shanghai dialects, has extensive commercial experience, is proficient in abacus and Chinese bookkeeping, and has experience in hardware stores, electrical appliance stores, and cigarette companies. Those in various industries who need such personnel are welcome to contact him. Salary is negotiable, and he has a reliable guarantor. Contact Mr. Ye, Room 209, 3rd Floor, Xingye Lane, Catholic Church Street, French Concession.

Opening Chapter [Long Life]

Longevity is the first of the five blessings in life. Today, a grand longevity banquet is held, with red longevity screens embroidered with gold characters, longevity couplets hung with famous calligraphy, immortal cranes calling in a longevity celebration, the God of Longevity and the Queen Mother greeting each other, and only the crane art adds to the longevity. New-style longevity cakes in the shape of peaches, wishing for virtuous descendants, brilliant longevity candles illuminating the scene, longevity incense burning, forming auspicious smoke, pairs of longevity shoes glittering, pairs of longevity dishes colorful and fresh, on the top is a vase of longevity chrysanthemums, and on the bottom are ancient and modern writings on longevity, delicious food and wine filling the banquet, celebrating longevity with family, and wishing for endless longevity noodles. It is truly a prosperous time for longevity, with endless joy and happiness, and the host enjoys both blessings and longevity.

Man Jiang Hong

Yu Shuicun is now with Liang Qiushan and the others. He feels satisfied with this environment. Although he can't live in luxury, he can definitely practice the attitude of [a commoner can be proud of princes and dukes]. This proves the dignity of the artist!

Qiushan relies on selling articles for income!

Xinye is a quasi-photographer. He carries a camera to the mountains every day to capture scenes, but he doesn't take pictures because he has run out of film!

The life of an artist is so natural and so optimistic!

Minsheng Drama Club New Voice (1380) 10:00 PM to 11:00 PM

Two Orphan Girls at the End of the World

Chen Dalong is the orderly of a certain general. The general left for the front line. Chen did not follow him. The general has a wife, Sun, who was seduced by Dalong and lost her virginity. Sun became pregnant. After ten months, she gave birth to a daughter. Suddenly, she received a telegram from the general saying that he would be home soon. She was shocked and plotted with Dalong to abandon the daughter. If someone takes her in, mother and son may meet one day. Dalong immediately took the daughter away.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

John Barrymore's Strange Illness (Part 2) 208

— Yi An

The natives said he was cursed by [Condor]

The doctors are helpless and fear that he will no longer be able to make movies

Although John Barrymore's health is far from what it used to be, he heard the doctor say that he was getting better, so he actively started working again. This spring, he filled a car with travel equipment and took his wife and two children to the mountains of Yucymytos to play. He slept outdoors at the foot of the mountain and ate in the shade of the trees. The doctors thought that was his only chance to regain his health. When he came back, he immediately started working, shooting the Columbia Company's [Twentieth Century Express]. Because he was plagued by illness and the work was too hard, by the time the director finally called [Cut!], he was too weak to stand. So he immediately took his wife and children on his large yacht and went to rest in the Alaskan Pacific Ocean. That was his first time in the Alaskan sea. He caught salmon and played with bears there. After a while, he came back again. When he came back, he passed through the harbor of Wen Guhua, so he ordered the anchor to be dropped there, took out his fishing gear, and fished there. Unexpectedly, while he was baiting, his finger was pricked by a fishhook. By the time he returned to Los Angeles, the finger had festered. When his finger was first pricked, his wife, Doris Costello, had treated him initially, but it didn't help. His hand continued to swell, and the pain gradually increased. His body temperature also rose day by day. At first, he was confined to bed. After a period of treatment, he felt better and could leave the bed. So he listened to the doctor again, got back on his big yacht, and set off for a long-term rest in the Alaskan sea. That was his most recent trip.

The doctors told John Barrymore that even if he felt better, he should not immediately resume work. However, everyone knows that the Barrymore family is one of the most hardworking and able to endure suffering. John's brother, Lionel Barrymore, suffered from painful, swollen rheumatism for almost sixteen years, with both legs behaving like paralysis. In those sixteen years, he never had a moment free from pain. His sister, Ethel Barrymore, also suffered from endless pain from time to time. She suffered from arthritis, and her kneecaps and other joints swelled up from time to time, causing her unspeakable suffering. Although her illness has not been cured, she still performs on stage in London every day.

If John Barrymore never made another movie, of course, it would not have any impact on him economically. All his equipment has been arranged in advance, so he will not feel materially deficient again. He was very poor when he was young, so his preparations were particularly thorough. He grew up in a family of actors, but his family was very poor. When he was sixteen, he ran away from school to study art. Because his father thought he had an inclination for art, he scraped together some money and sent him to France to study oil painting. Soon he ran out of money and returned dejectedly. He worked as an illustrator at a newspaper in New York, but he was soon unemployed again. In his poverty and boredom, he returned to his grandfather's career as an actor, but it took a long time to gain some recognition in the theater world. Ever since he arrived in Hollywood, his luck has turned around, and he has been able to turn everything he touches into gold. Soon he accumulated millions of dollars. In addition, he is good at management, and he can never worry about poverty in his life.

A Condor bird, [Malangni], although locked in a cage, can control the fate of its owner and bestow upon him the blessings and misfortunes he deserves, as the natives of Galapagos say—to ask John Barrymore whether he believes such absurd and unfounded words, he would definitely say [Tut-tut—] but Malangni is always his companion. He carries it with him, feeds it himself, and treats it like his friend—he never abandons a friend. (The End)

Film Commentary

Review of [Fallen]—Jin Cheng 209

— Ling He

In any case, the level of Chinese films has improved. This is how I felt when I saw [Fallen]. Of course, we don't say that this is a completely successful work, but under small-scale management, we see that the creators of this film (from the director and photographer to the actors) are working so hard and so sincerely on the art of film, which is worthy of our joy. Moreover, this film has good results in individual parts.

We can say that this and [Song of the Fishermen] have some similarities, at least in terms of subject matter. However, the subject matter here is too realistic at present, so the author of [Song of the Fishermen] can hear it, and the author of [Fallen] can also see it.

It is very obvious that the creators of [Fallen] are very sympathetic to the poor masses, and at the same time, they are very disgusted with the lascivious lives of the crumbling rich. So he used the method of comparing the rich and the poor to unfold two different lives before our eyes, so the tragedy of the poor won the sympathy of the audience.

Of course, in many cases, the lack of expression methods is revealed, that is, there is no appropriate technique to express what they want to say through the art of film. The main thing is that the story is too long and too much, so that only a very long story is heard, and not much of the dramatic part is seen. Secondly, the playwright has too little organizational power, and there is no way to organize a lengthy story. At the beginning, two lines were unfolded at the same time, and a nanny brought the two lines together, but when writing about the third generation, we saw that the playwright had no power to closely develop the two aspects to the end. Here, except for the fact that the young lady of the rich family ran over the coolie of the poor family with a car (of course, this was very accidental), there was almost no relationship between the two. Moreover, in the end, the side of the rich was simply abandoned. Only the side of the poor was seen, desperately stretching the story.

We have to point out that there are too many themes grabbed here, and the film of ten thousand feet or so simply cannot accommodate them. Moreover, there is no center of gravity, and the result is that many materials are displayed in a disorderly manner.

The playwright only superficially grasps social phenomena, without uncovering the essence. So he only understands the rich people's desire for pleasure in warmth and fullness, and the poor people's sad lives. The rich people's sins contrast with the poor people's suffering, but he lightly lets go of the broken hands of the Jiuhua Yarn Factory and the car accident that killed Yongfu, etc. (Of course, there is a relationship of inspection here.) In this way, only the tragic fate of the poor is seen, and the growth of tomorrow is seen in today's China, which becomes the regret of the work, although the playwright pointed out the collapse of the rich.

The playwright's grasp of the central consciousness is fully expressed from the beginning when writing about Yinmei's lasciviousness to later when he quite sympathizes with her. As for the unclear introduction of the characters, such as the appearance of the neighbor being too strange, etc., there are more small mistakes, such as when Tang Xueqian is crazy, she clearly shouts A Qiao, why doesn't Fan Xuepeng know that she is his own mother?

For the meaning of [the Spring and Autumn Annals blames the wise], we have pointed out a lot about the script. At the same time, we find the playwright's efforts to improve and vividly depict reality commendable. Moreover, the playwright's intelligence is manifested in many places.

Although we say that the above points are the responsibility of the playwright, the director cannot have good editing, does not know how to be economical, and cannot reasonably grasp the dramatic parts and give full play to them, while some parts are stretched too long, which are the reasons why the work is not brilliant. However, the director is very hardworking. He treats every scene very sincerely, but he is not able to grasp the dramatic effect. There are several good scenes here, such as the collapsed car falling in the mud, the machines in the factory injuring people at that time, and Yongfu's death. If it could be more economical, it would be very commendable. As for the relatively lively camera movements and the guidance of acting, he also works very hard. If Tang Xueqian packs her baggage and wipes her tears with the corner of the cloth, the long shot and the medium shot are repeated, which shows his poor editing.

Among the actors, Li Ying, Fan Xuepeng, Tang Xueqian, and Wen Zhiyu are better, as well as the neighbor's man and the prostitute's introducer (the woman with gold teeth). Although there are very few scenes, they are very realistic. The set designers and photographers have quite good results.

Audience Opinions

Reflections After Watching "The Way of Women" 210

— Yafei

This is a film recommended by dozens of educators and praised by Shanghai children for its happiness. It takes family and education as its themes. Indeed, the influence of family education on children is very important. Women are the backbone of every family, so they have the closest direct responsibility for family education. Therefore, recently, countries around the world have been advocating the idea of "virtuous mothers and good wives." For example, the Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, he is an ardent advocate of the "virtuous mother and good wife" system. "To love a thing immoderately is to harm it," this is also a wake-up call for those who dote on their children without understanding!

"The Way of Women" is a film that emerges on the theme of family education, but it does not have a thorough understanding of family education. The story is very ordinary, and the screenwriter's avoidance of the important and dwelling on the trivial in modern children's education is, of course, undeniable. He wrote about Baosheng's love of sweets, so he repeatedly showed him chewing sugar on the screen, especially ending with closing the window, which clearly shows the screenwriter's cowardice.

The director, Chen Kengran, is very dedicated in this film. He handles the story in a very organized manner, which greatly helps the development of the plot. The angles of several shots are also used very cleverly.

In terms of actors, Xu Qinfang powerfully portrays a "virtuous mother." Hu Yixing is also a very good talent, but it is a pity that the director did not use him correctly here. The other actors are generally passable.

Film is generally recognized as the eighth art, and it bears the mission of social education, so we are definitely not just running to the cinema for entertainment for two hours. We want to have more important educational significance in addition to entertainment.

Submission Guidelines for Shen Bao Film Supplement 212

This publication is a film publication that assists in the promotion of culture and art. It welcomes contributions from both foreign and domestic sources. Once published, remuneration will be generous.

Once a text is published and paid for, the copyright belongs to Shen Bao.

The text of this publication should be mainly in vernacular Chinese and must use modern punctuation.

If the submission is a translation, please attach the original. English should be used sparingly if it can be omitted.

Do not write or draw on both sides of the manuscript paper, or write horizontally, and do not use a pencil.

The length of this publication is limited, so the text should be as concise as possible. Each manuscript should be limited to about 500 words.

When submitting a manuscript, each piece must have a seal, otherwise, the remuneration will be rejected.

Film Novel

Meeting Too Late (The Age of Innocence) (Part Two) 213

— Li Xin

Newland smiled at Mrs. Mingott with sympathy. For more than a decade, she had been the female czar of New York society. With her protection, who would dare to spread rumors and make trouble for Ellen? The next day, Newland Archer sat in his law office, waiting for Ellen to come in. He was the youngest member of the law firm of Letterblair, Lamson, and Low, so all the cases that the older partners didn't want to take were handed over to him. But this time, he was very satisfied with accepting Ellen's commission, although he couldn't help but feel some trepidation. Soon, Ellen arrived, and Newland looked at her and felt that she had a different kind of charm than the night before, even more beautiful than he could remember. Her beauty was alive, constantly renewing, and emanating from within, he thought. He sat across from her, and while he was flipping through the documents, he was wondering what made her so different from other women. He thought about it, and the first thing was her dress—simple and quiet. Compared to other women, he felt that they were dressed too luxuriously and decorated excessively, which made them seem vulgar. But it wasn't just about clothing. Her inner peace was also what made her different from others. Compared to her, others seemed either noisy or dull. Ellen said, "I've rented a house on Twenty-third Street." Newland expressed surprise and said, "Rent a house? Alone?" Ellen said, "Of course. That's the only way. I understand my relatives' attitude towards me—they're all the same, except for Mrs. Mingott. But, Newland, I'd rather be free." She smiled again and said, "When I've finished decorating in a few days, won't you come and see it? Come with May?"

A few days later, Newland did go to see her new house, but he went alone. After that, he went to Ellen's house every day, as if he had official business every day and Ellen had documents to sign every day. Ellen's new home, like her personality, had a special simple charm and a kind of warm, pleasant, quiet taste. There, one could find spiritual rest and soulful enjoyment, which was clearly different from the magnificent, wealth-pressuring atmosphere of other places. One day, he was on his way to Ellen's house when he passed a flower shop and saw a bunch of special roses—the petals were particularly deep and the color was particularly bright. He thought that they were the flowers for Ellen, so he bought them and took them to Ellen's house. When he arrived at Ellen's house, he gave her the flowers and stood in front of the fireplace, silently watching her put the flowers in a vase. He suddenly had a feeling and said, "Ellen, you shouldn't live outside alone. You should think about your family, those who love you, those who are willing to protect you." Ellen listened and looked at him strangely, saying, "Newland, I often think about them too. But—those women—they won't understand—because they've never felt—that need." Newland didn't understand and said, "Need?" Ellen sighed and said, "Yes, Newland. Please don't reject me from a thousand miles away like others do. It seems that no one here is willing to be realistic. They're all pretending—" She suddenly couldn't continue, she stared at Newland, and then said, "Newland, some women are content with an ordinary life, but I don't want to hide it from you. I am a special woman, and I must have love—I must be loved... Are you thinking that I am too... what, after I said this?" Newland quickly said, "No... I think that's very upright and admirable. I have never met a woman who can talk so frankly." Ellen said, "Newland, thank you, luckily you are still a sensible person." He slowly walked over, put his hand on her shoulder, and looked down at her eyebrows. His head slowly lowered, hugged her tightly, and kissed her fragrant lips, kissing her fully. At first, she couldn't help but press her delicate body tightly against him, letting him kiss her, but after a while, she stretched out a hand, weakly waving, trying to push him away. She panicked and said, "Go, Newland," she sobbed, "You'd better go now." She didn't wait for him to speak, had already turned around and ran upstairs. (To be continued)
